{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"This Week in Apps: Conservative apps surge, Instagram redesigned, TikTok gets ghosted","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073685","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Welcome back to This Week in Apps, the TechCrunch series that recaps the latest OS news, the applications they support and the money that flows through it all.</p>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The app industry is as hot as ever, with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/15/app-stores-saw-record-204-billion-app-downloads-in-2019-consumer-spend-of-120-billion/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a record</a> 204 billion downloads and $120 billion in consumer spending in 2019. People are now <a href=\"https://www.emarketer.com/content/average-us-time-spent-with-mobile-in-2019-has-increased\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">spending</a> three hours and 40 minutes per day using apps, rivaling TV. Apps aren’t just a way to pass idle hours — they’re a big business. In 2019, mobile-first companies had a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/15/app-stores-saw-record-204-billion-app-downloads-in-2019-consumer-spend-of-120-billion/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">combined</a> $544 billion valuation, 6.5x higher than those without a mobile focus.</p>\n<h1>Top Stories</h1>\n<h2>Trump administration backs down on TikTok ban</h2>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><div id=\"attachment_2064682\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2064682\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2064682\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/GettyImages-1229058759.jpeg?w=680\" alt=\"CULVER CITY, CA - OCTOBER 13: General view of the TikTok headquarters on October 13, 2020 in Culver City, California. (Photo by AaronP/Bauer-Griffin/GC Images)\" width=\"680\" height=\"454\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/GettyImages-1229058759.jpeg 1024w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/GettyImages-1229058759.jpeg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/GettyImages-1229058759.jpeg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/GettyImages-1229058759.jpeg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/GettyImages-1229058759.jpeg?resize=680,454 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/GettyImages-1229058759.jpeg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2064682\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Photo by AaronP/Bauer-Griffin/GC Images)</p></div></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The Trump administration seemingly forgot it had banned the TikTok app in the U.S., as the president focused this week instead on sowing doubt over the integrity of the U.S. elections &#8212; which the Dept. of Homeland Security<a href=\"https://www.axios.com/cisa-election-security-trump-a385868b-512a-4449-addd-4591829a4aef.html\"> just called</a> the &#8220;most secure in American History,&#8221; by the way.</p>\n<p>The inaction on the Trump administration&#8217;s part revealed what many suspected all along: that the TikTok ban was largely performative.</p>\n<p>Earlier this week, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/bytedance-asks-federal-appeals-court-to-vacate-u-s-order-forcing-it-to-sell-tiktok/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\">TikTok went public with the fact</a> that it hadn&#8217;t heard anything about its ban for weeks, despite the fact that it had a deadline of November 12 to divest its U.S. assets. <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/11/10/what-happened-to-tiktok-deal-trump-administration-silent.html\">The company filed a petition</a> in the U.S. Court of Appeals for the D.C. Circuit on Tuesday, calling for a review of actions by CFIUS (Trump’s committee on foreign investment in the United States).</p>\n<p>TikTok had earlier asked for an extension, but never heard back, it said.</p>\n<p>Or, as the winning headline put it, <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/11/10/21559677/tiktok-cfius-court-petition-ban-deadline\">courtesy of The Verge</a>: &#8220;TikTok says the Trump administration has forgotten about trying to ban it, would like to know what’s up.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In a statement, TikTok said:</p>\n<p><em>&#8220;For a year, TikTok has actively engaged with CFIUS in good faith to address its national security concerns, even as we disagree with its assessment. In the nearly two months since the President gave his preliminary approval to our proposal to satisfy those concerns, we have offered detailed solutions to finalize that agreement – but have received no substantive feedback on our extensive data privacy and security framework.</em></p>\n<p><em>Facing continual new requests and no clarity on whether our proposed solutions would be accepted, we requested the 30-day extension that is expressly permitted in the August 14 order. Today, with the November 12 CFIUS deadline imminent and without an extension in hand, we have no choice but to file a petition in court to defend our rights and those of our more than 1,500 employees in the US. We remain committed to working with the Administration — as we have all along — to resolve the issues it has raised, but our legal challenge today is a protection to ensure these discussions can take place.&#8221;</em></p>\n<p>After getting the reminder, the Commerce Dept. on Thursday said it wouldn&#8217;t enforce the order that required TikTok to shut down, citing a preliminary injunction against the shutdown last month that came about as a result <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/30/tiktok-stars-got-a-judge-to-block-trumps-tiktok-ban/\">of the lawsuit by TikTok stars</a>, who claimed the app&#8217;s closure would impact their ability to make an income. However, it also appealed that same ruling, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/the-u-s-government-sends-mixed-messages-about-tiktoks-future/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\">leading to further confusion.</a></p>\n<p>The question now is how will the incoming <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2020/11/12/cybersecurity-202-biden-administration-could-mean-reset-us-war-tiktok/\">Biden administration proceed</a> with regard to the Trump TikTok ban. Though Biden has criticized Trump&#8217;s China policy, concern over TikTok was one that saw bipartisan support. Biden even said <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-tiktok-ban-biden/biden-says-he-sees-tiktok-as-a-matter-of-genuine-concern-idUSKBN26938G\">during a campaign stop in September</a> that it was worrisome that a Chinese operation would have access to over 100 million young people in the U.S.</p>\n<h2>Election results send conservative apps up the charts</h2>\n<p>After a nerve-wracking week of election results which devolved into political chaos as Trump rallied his base to believe <a href=\"https://www.cisa.gov/news/2020/11/12/joint-statement-elections-infrastructure-government-coordinating-council-election\">baseless</a> claims of fraud, a number of right-wing Trump supporters turned to alternative apps for social media and news.</p>\n<p>The App Store&#8217;s top charts, which are determined by a combination of downloads and velocity, among other factors, soon featured a new set of alternative apps, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/parler-app-store-facebook/\">led by</a> free speech network Parler, which found itself in the No. 1 spot. (It&#8217;s since slipped thanks to Walmart&#8217;s Black Friday <a href=\"https://www.cnet.com/news/black-friday-walmart-deals-available-now-99-cordless-vacuum-194-airpods-pro-and-more/\">sales</a>, which sent the retailer&#8217;s app flying up to No. 1.)</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073831\" style=\"width: 339px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073831\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2073831\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg?w=329\" alt=\"\" width=\"329\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg 1125w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg?resize=73,150 73w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg?resize=145,300 145w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg?resize=768,1587 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg?resize=329,680 329w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg?resize=743,1536 743w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg?resize=991,2048 991w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/IMG_6490.jpg?resize=24,50 24w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 329px) 100vw, 329px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2073831\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Screenshot from App Store</p></div></p>\n<p>According <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/11/9/21557219/parler-conservative-app-download-new-users-moderation-bias\">to one estimate</a>, Parler saw 980K downloads from November 3 through November 8. <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/11/technology/parler-rumble-newsmax.html\">Other apps</a> also benefitted from the election drama, including social network MeWe (now No. 10 on the iPhone Top Free Apps chart in the U.S. and right-wing news network Newsmax TV (No. 7).</p>\n<p>Unlike Facebook and Twitter &#8212; which increasingly use fact-checking services to label or, in extreme cases, hide false claims behind an extra click &#8212; alternative apps do not. But they are not neutral platforms by any means. The verified account from &#8220;Team Trump&#8221; was <a href=\"https://www.wired.com/story/parler-app-free-speech-influencers/\">among those that automatically greeted</a> new Parler users, for example. Right-wing politicians like senator Ted Cruz and representative Devin Nunes as well as other conservative personalities have set up shop on Parler, too.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"dXGK9CFD31\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/parler-app-store-facebook/\">&#8216;Free speech&#8217; social network Parler tops app store rankings following Biden&#8217;s election win</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;&#8216;Free speech&#8217; social network Parler tops app store rankings following Biden&#8217;s election win&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/parler-app-store-facebook/embed/#?secret=dXGK9CFD31\" data-secret=\"dXGK9CFD31\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>As a result, the community is lopsided. Users are posting to amplify their beliefs among those who largely feel the same as they do. And, because Parler does not combat misinformation and conspiracy theories with fact-checking, it&#8217;s already been targeted by a conspiracy theory of its very own. A Photoshopped image of a Fox News ticker spread confusion on Parler this week, as the modified image claimed that George Soros owned the social network. The conspiracy got enough traction that Parler founder John Matze had to post that it was not true. But Parler&#8217;s true origins and ownership are still being discussed.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s unclear to what extent the conservative apps represent a new wave of social media with long-term staying power, given that any relative newcomer to the space will still ultimately have to compete with very large networks, like Facebook&#8217;s 2 billion users. Though smaller than Facebook, Twitter&#8217;s 330 million monthly active users is still much larger than Parler&#8217;s monthly active user base <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/tech/tech-news/twitter-conservatives-parler-surges-amid-election-misinformation-crackdown-n1247333\">of about 4 million</a> (its active users are around half of its registered users, which is now 8 million.)</p>\n<p>Larger platforms have resources to pour into more than just the basics of keeping the servers running. And, to date, that&#8217;s led to the demise of numerous other would-be Facebook rivals. The few apps that manage to grow a following these days are those that get a majority of younger, mainstream users, like TikTok and Snapchat.</p>\n<p>Regardless of your political leanings, I think we can all agree there was a lot of this going on this week:</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2073829\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/38FzXsA.jpg?w=539\" alt=\"\" width=\"539\" height=\"614\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/38FzXsA.jpg 539w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/38FzXsA.jpg?resize=132,150 132w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/38FzXsA.jpg?resize=263,300 263w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/38FzXsA.jpg?resize=44,50 44w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 539px) 100vw, 539px\" /></p>\n<h2>Instagram Redesign</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2072808\" 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Launch-Image-Home-Reels-Shop.png?resize=300,191 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Launch-Image-Home-Reels-Shop.png?resize=768,490 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Launch-Image-Home-Reels-Shop.png?resize=2048,1307 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Launch-Image-Home-Reels-Shop.png?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2072808\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Instagram</p></div></p>\n<p>Instagram this week put its TikTok competitor Reels front-and-center in a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/instagram-redesign-puts-reels-and-shop-tabs-on-the-home-screen/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\">redesigned version of its app</a> by giving it the center position on its new navigation bar. The update also replaced the Activity tab (heart icon) with the Shop tab, following a test that had changed this aspect of the app’s home screen earlier this summer. And it revamped the Camera interface and did away with the IGTV button.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"EXXdCJZ1un\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/instagram-redesign-puts-reels-and-shop-tabs-on-the-home-screen/\">Instagram redesign puts Reels and Shop tabs on the home screen</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Instagram redesign puts Reels and Shop tabs on the home screen&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/instagram-redesign-puts-reels-and-shop-tabs-on-the-home-screen/embed/#?secret=EXXdCJZ1un\" data-secret=\"EXXdCJZ1un\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>In the redesigned app, both the Compose button and the Activity tab have been relocated to the top-right of the home screen, while the center middle button now belongs to Reels.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2072810\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2072810\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2072810\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png 1080w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png?resize=150,150 https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png?resize=680,680 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png?resize=32,32 32w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png?resize=50,50 50w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png?resize=64,64 64w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png?resize=96,96 96w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Unified-Camera.png?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2072810\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Instagram</p></div></p>\n<p>The redesign is an aggressive attempt on Instagram’s part to direct users to its short-form video feed, Reels, which has so far seen only a lukewarm reception from reviewers, who have called it stale, lacking in effects and another contributor to Instagram bloat.</p>\n<p>The changes were also a big push to make the Instagram app more of an online shopping destination at a critical time for the e-commerce market. The coronavirus pandemic <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/24/covid-19-pandemic-accelerated-shift-to-e-commerce-by-5-years-new-report-says/\">accelerated the shift to e-commerce by at least five years</a>, according to some analysts. That means any plans Instagram had to become a major player in online commerce were also just expedited.</p>\n<p>Both moves signal a company that’s worried about the impact TikTok may have on the long-term future of its business. TikTok <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/new-forecast-pegs-tiktok-to-top-1-2b-monthly-active-users-in-2021/\">is now projected to top 1.2 billion monthly active users in 2021</a>. And <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/27/tiktok-invests-in-social-commerce-via-new-shopify-partnership/\">as its recent partnership with Shopify on social commerce</a> indicates, it could be a new home for social commerce soon too.</p>\n<h1>Weekly News</h1>\n<h2>Platforms</h2>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Apple at its Mac event detailed that its <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/ios-apps-can-run-on-apples-new-apple-silicon-macs/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\">new Apple Silicon Macs would be able to run iOS apps.</a> </strong>The news was first announced at WWDC, but is now officially going to roll out with Big Sur and the new Macs. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> showed off Among Us and HBO Max apps during a demo, but it&#8217;s unclear if others are being <a href=\"https://9to5mac.com/2020/11/09/ios-apps-will-run-on-apple-silicon-macs-but-major-developers-have-already-opted-out-of-the-mac-app-store/\">allowed</a> to opt out.</li>\n<li><strong>Apple&#8217;s TestFlight</strong> beta testing app <a href=\"https://9to5mac.com/2020/11/11/testflight-automatic-updates/\">now supports</a> automatic updates. At last!</li>\n<li><strong>iOS 14.3</strong> and iPadOS 14.3 beta 1 releases <a href=\"https://www.iphonehacks.com/2020/11/ios-14-3-ipados-14-3-beta-1-download.html\">arrived</a>.</li>\n<li><strong>Android <a href=\"https://siliconangle.com/2020/11/12/androids-neural-networks-api-adds-support-pytorch-enable-device-ai-processing/\">added</a> support for PyTorch</strong> for on-device AI processing.</li>\n<li><strong>Epic Games scores a point in the App Store legal battle</strong> over in-app purchase fees. A <a href=\"http://www.fosspatents.com/2020/11/court-throws-out-tort-based-part-of.html\">judge dismissed Apple&#8217;s claims</a> that Epic&#8217;s actions were wrong, which reduces the potential risk of its lawsuit, limiting Apple&#8217;s counterclaims to breach of contract. (Punitive damages have not yet been discussed.)</li>\n<li><strong>Apple to suggest third-party apps during setup</strong>, with iOS 14.3, <a href=\"https://9to5mac.com/2020/11/12/ios-14-3-will-suggest-third-party-apps-to-users-during-the-iphone-or-ipad-setup-process/\">according to details found in the app&#8217;s code</a>. This appears to be there for compliance with local laws in select countries where antitrust issues are a concern.</li>\n<li><strong>Android Enterprise Recommended program adds Samsung and others</strong>. The program, launched in 2018, helps enterprise customers evaluate and approve devices that meet Google’s requirements for hardware, software and updates.<a href=\"https://blog.google/products/android-enterprise/android-enterprise-recommended-new-partners/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+blogspot%2FMKuf+%28The+Keyword+%7C+Official+Google+Blog%29\"> This change brings</a> Samsung Galaxy devices and others into the fold.</li>\n<li><strong>Time to vote for Google Play&#8217;s &#8220;Best of 2020.&#8221;</strong> You can vote through November 23 to <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/editorial_collection/promotion_topic_bestof2020_uv_hub\">help pick Google&#8217;s Users&#8217; Choice winners</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5W1kCEcs7S\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/ios-apps-can-run-on-apples-new-apple-silicon-macs/\">iOS apps can run on Apple&#8217;s new Apple Silicon Macs</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;iOS apps can run on Apple&#8217;s new Apple Silicon Macs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/ios-apps-can-run-on-apples-new-apple-silicon-macs/embed/#?secret=5W1kCEcs7S\" data-secret=\"5W1kCEcs7S\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<h2><strong>Security &#38; Privacy</strong></h2>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Zoom <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/zoom-ftc-deceptive-security-claims/\">settled with FTC</a> after making deceptive security claims.</strong> The company had claimed its video calls were protected by “end-to-end” encryption that made it impossible for anyone, including Zoom to listen in. This wasn&#8217;t true, as Zoom maintained the cryptographic keys that could allow it to access the content of its customers’ meetings.</li>\n</ul>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"9PNtgh3WSw\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/zoom-ftc-deceptive-security-claims/\">Zoom settles with FTC after making &#8216;deceptive&#8217; security claims</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Zoom settles with FTC after making &#8216;deceptive&#8217; feature</a> that lets you enable disappearing messages from within a conversation. The upgrade on Instagram is only part of the big <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/30/facebook-introduces-cross-app-communication-between-messenger-and-instagram-plus-other-features/\">messaging update</a> that unifies the inbox with Facebook.</li>\n<li><strong>Apple cracked down on iOS terminal apps</strong>. a-Shell and iSH, two terminal apps popular with developers, were blocked from the App Store because they&#8230;drum roll&#8230;execute scripts. Oh c&#8217;mon, Apple. <a href=\"https://www.macworld.com/article/3596395/oops-they-did-it-again-more-app-store-follies.html#tk.rss_all\">iSH appealed</a> and was returned to the App Store. a-Shell has <a href=\"https://twitter.com/a_Shell_iOS/status/1325526061099196416\">appealed as well</a>. Apple ended up <a href=\"https://appleinsider.com/articles/20/11/09/apple-backtracks-on-app-store-removal-threat-for-unix-shell-ios-apps\">apologizing.</a></li>\n<li><strong>No more free storage for your Google Photos</strong>. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> this week said all your photo uploads <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/11/google-cuts-back-on-its-free-storage-get-ready-to-pay-up/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\">will now count towards</a> your Google account&#8217;s 15GB of free storage. Get ready to pay for <a href=\"https://one.google.com/\">Google One</a>.</li>\n<li><strong>TikTok expands fundraising features.</strong> The company already allowed users to fundraise from donation stickers. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/11/tiktok-test-lets-users-fundraise-for-charity-from-their-profile/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\">Now you can do so</a> directly from your profile, too.</li>\n<li><strong>Disney+ app reaches 100M+ global downloads</strong>, with 62% coming from the U.S., <a href=\"https://blog.apptopia.com/disney-reaches-100m-downloads-and-285m-iap-revenue-in-its-first-year\">according to Apptopia data. </a></li>\n<li><strong>TikTok to top 1.2B MAUs by 2021</strong>, per<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/new-forecast-pegs-tiktok-to-top-1-2b-monthly-active-users-in-2021/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\"> App Annie&#8217;s forecast</a>.</li>\n<li><strong>Bumble&#8217;s<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/bumbles-new-feature-prevents-bad-actors-from-using-unmatch-to-hide-from-their-victims/?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\"> new feature</a> prevents bad actors from using &#8220;unmatch&#8221; to avoid being reported for harassment and other issues. </strong>The change came following <a href=\"https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-10-12/tinder-dating-app-helps-sexual-predators-hide-four-corners/12722732?nw=0\">reports of victims of harassment and crime</a>, including rape, were unable to report their abusers because they had unmatched their victims.</li>\n<li><strong>Zynga <a href=\"https://www.businessofapps.com/news/zynga-revenues-jump-46-amid-more-mobile-gamers-playing-during-lockdowns/\">recorded</a> a 46% rise in revenue in Q3 2020</strong>, to reach $503 million, an increase in DAUs of 53% to 31 million, and a 23% increase in MAUs to 83 million.</li>\n</ul>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"61cU211ywy\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/bumbles-new-feature-prevents-bad-actors-from-using-unmatch-to-hide-from-their-victims/\">Bumble&#8217;s new feature prevents bad actors from using &#8216;unmatch&#8217; eds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn15@2020_1/2020/11/15/06-19-06-004_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn10@2020_3/2020/11/15/06-19-03-843_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=7jbBrcZqMjw:sYEXdkkuufc:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn70@2020_2/2020/11/15/06-19-04-756_b7a0cf02467f7e58.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=7jbBrcZqMjw:sYEXdkkuufc:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn89@2020_4/2020/11/15/06-19-05-394_e248ded51cb7161b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn52@2020_4/2020/11/15/06-19-06-130_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/7jbBrcZqMjw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn29@2020_6/2020/11/15/06-19-03-870_399cd6e6b7de76a3.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605421118998},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"Uber in talks to sell ATG self-driving unit to Aurora","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073883","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Eighteen months ago, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/uber\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"uber\">Uber’s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> self-driving car unit, Uber Advanced Technologies Group, was valued at $7.25 billion following a $1 billion investment from Toyota, DENSO and SoftBank’s Vision Fund. Now, it’s up for sale and a competing autonomous vehicle technology startup is in talks with Uber to buy it, according to three sources familiar with the deal.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/aurora-innovation\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"aurora-innovation\">Aurora Innovation, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> the startup founded by three veterans of the autonomous vehicle industry who led programs at Google, Tesla and Uber, is in negotiations to buy Uber ATG. Terms of the deal are still unknown, but sources say the two companies have been in talks since October and it is far along in the process.</p>\n<p>An Uber spokesperson declined to comment, citing that the company&#8217;s general policy is not to comment on these sorts of inquiries. An Aurora spokesperson said it doesn&#8217;t comment on speculation.</p>\n<p>The talks could falter. But if successful, they have the potential to triple Aurora’s headcount and allow Uber to unload an expensive long-term play that has sustained several controversies in its short life.</p>\n<h2>Uber has &#8216;been shopping&#8217;</h2>\n<p>Shedding Uber ATG would follow a string of spin-offs or other deals in recent months that has narrowed Uber’s focus and costs into core areas of ride-hailing and delivery. Two years ago, Uber’s business model could be described as an &#8220;all of the above approach,&#8221; a bet on generating revenue from all forms of transportation, including ride-hailing, micromobility, logistics, package and food delivery and someday even autonomous robotaxis.</p>\n<p>That strategy has changed since Uber went public and has further accelerated as the COVID-19 pandemic has upended the economy and fundamentally changed how people live. In the past 11 months, Uber has dumped shared micromobility unit Jump, sold a stake in its growing but still unprofitable logistics arm, Uber Freight and acquired Postmates. (The Postmates acquisition is expected to close in the fourth quarter of 2020).</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"MmW5voxBUd\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/07/uber-leads-170-million-lime-investment-offloads-jump-to-lime/\">Uber leads $170M Lime investment, offloads Jump to Lime</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Uber leads $170M Lime investment, offloads Jump to Lime&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/07/uber-leads-170-million-lime-investment-offloads-jump-to-lime/embed/#?secret=MmW5voxBUd\" data-secret=\"MmW5voxBUd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Uber ATG has been the company’s last big, expensive holding. Uber ATG holds a lot of long-term promise and high present-day costs; Uber reported in November that ATG and &#8220;other technologies&#8221; (which includes Uber Elevate) had a net loss of $303 million in the nine months that ended September 30, 2020. In its S-1 document, Uber said it incurred $457 million of research and development expenses for its ATG and &#8220;other Technology Programs&#8221; initiatives.</p>\n<p>Four sources within the industry told TechCrunch that Uber “has been shopping” ATG to several companies, including automakers this year. Sources have also told TechCrunch that Uber ATG was facing a potential down round, which might have been an additional motivator behind the talks with Aurora.</p>\n<p>Aurora, which was founded in 2017, is focused on building the full self-driving stack, the underlying technology that will allow vehicles to navigate highways and city streets without a human driver behind the wheel. Aurora has attracted attention and investment from high-profile venture firms, management firms and corporations such as Greylock Partners, Sequoia Capital, Amazon and T. Rowe Price, in part because of its founders Sterling Anderson, Drew Bagnell and Chris Urmson.</p>\n<p>Urmson led the former Google self-driving project before it spun out to become the Alphabet business Waymo. Anderson is best known for leading the development and launch of the Tesla Model X and the automaker&#8217;s Autopilot program. Bagnell, an associate professor at Carnegie Mellon, helped launch Uber&#8217;s efforts in autonomy, ultimately heading the autonomy and perception team at the Advanced Technologies Center in Pittsburgh.</p>\n<p>Aurora has grown from a small upstart to a company with 600 employees and operations in the San Francisco Bay Area, Pittsburgh, Texas and Bozeman, Montana, home of Blackmore, the lidar company it acquired in 2019. About 12% of Aurora’s current workforce previously worked at Uber, according to records on LinkedIn.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"eHbzXcaEaa\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/05/23/fresh-off-a-530m-round-aurora-acquires-lidar-startup-blackmore/\">Fresh off a $530M round, Aurora acquires lidar startup Blackmore</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Fresh off a $530M round, Aurora acquires lidar startup Blackmore&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/05/23/fresh-off-a-530m-round-aurora-acquires-lidar-startup-blackmore/embed/#?secret=eHbzXcaEaa\" data-secret=\"eHbzXcaEaa\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Despite that growth, Aurora is still dwarfed by Uber ATG, the self-driving subsidiary that is majority owned by Uber. Uber ATG has more than 1,200 employees with operations in several locations, including Pittsburgh, San Francisco and Toronto. Uber holds an 86.2% stake (on a fully diluted basis) in Uber ATG, according to filings with the <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1543151/000119312519188316/d767435d8k.htm\">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a>. Its investors hold a combined stake of 13.8% in Uber ATG.</p>\n<p>Uber’s public leap into autonomous vehicle technology began in earnest in early 2015 when the company announced a strategic partnership with Carnegie Mellon University’s National Robotics Center. The agreement to work on developing driverless car technology resulted in <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/is-uber-a-friend-or-foe-of-carnegie-mellon-in-robotics-1433084582\">Uber poaching dozens of NREC researchers</a> and scientists. <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A year later, with the beginnings of an in-house AV development program, Uber, then led by co-founder Travis Kalanick, acquired a self-driving truck startup called Otto.</span></p>\n<p>The acquisition was troubled almost from the start. Otto was founded earlier that year by one of Google’s star engineers, Anthony Levandowski, along with three other Google veterans: Lior Ron, Claire Delaunay and Don Burnette. Uber acquired Otto less than eight months later.</p>\n<p>Two months after the acquisition, Google made two arbitration demands against Levandowski and Ron. Uber wasn&#8217;t a party to either arbitration. While the arbitrations played out, Waymo separately filed a lawsuit against Uber in February 2017 for trade secret theft and patent infringement. Waymo alleged in the suit, which went to trial but ended in a settlement in 2018, that Levandowski stole trade secrets, which were then used by Uber.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"85PUJSILxx\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/02/09/uber-settles-lawsuit-with-waymo/\">Uber settles lawsuit with Waymo</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Uber settles lawsuit with Waymo&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/02/09/uber-settles-lawsuit-with-waymo/embed/#?secret=85PUJSILxx\" data-secret=\"85PUJSILxx\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Under the settlement, Uber agreed not to incorporate Waymo&#8217;s confidential information into their hardware and software. Uber also agreed to pay a financial settlement that included 0.34% of Uber equity, per its Series G-1 round $72 billion valuation. That was calculated at the time to be about $244.8 million in Uber equity.</p>\n<p>In the early days of the Otto acquisition, Uber estimated it could have 75,000 autonomous vehicles on the road by 2019 and be operating driverless taxi services in 13 cities by 2022, according to court documents unsealed and first reported on by TechCrunch. To reach those ambitious goals, the ride-hailing company was spending $20 million a month on developing self-driving technologies.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5DFlYrsHqK\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/03/12/ubers-self-driving-car-unit-was-burning-20-million-a-month/\">Uber&#8217;s self-driving car unit was burning $20 million a month</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Uber&#8217;s self-driving car unit was burning $20 million a month&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/03/12/ubers-self-driving-car-unit-was-burning-20-million-a-month/embed/#?secret=5DFlYrsHqK\" data-secret=\"5DFlYrsHqK\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Uber never came close to hitting those targets, a mission that was derailed by technical hurdles as well as the lawsuit with Waymo, its troubled relationship with Lewandowski and the fatal crash in March 2018 involving one of its self-driving test vehicles in Tempe, Arizona.</p>\n<p>Uber halted all testing following the crash and has been slowly ramping up its more public-facing operations over the past 18 months. The expensive undertaking of developing autonomous vehicles prompted Uber to spin out the company in spring 2019 after it closed $1 billion in funding from Toyota, auto parts maker Denso and SoftBank’s Vision Fund.</p>\n<p>The spin-out, which occurred about one month before Uber’s debut as a publicly traded company, had been the subject of speculation for months. It was seen as a way for Uber to share the expensive load with other investors and allow it to focus on its core competencies and nearer-term profit goals.</p>\n<h2>What Aurora gains</h2>\n<p>Troubles aside, Uber ATG has two important and critical features that make it attractive to Aurora: talent and Toyota.</p>\n<p>The Japanese car giant had already invested $500 million into Uber prior to the 2019 injection of cash. At the time, the two companies announced their intention to bring pilot-scale deployments of automated Toyota Sienna-based ridesharing vehicles to the Uber ridesharing network in 2021, “leveraging the strengths of Uber ATG’s self-driving technology alongside the Toyota Guardian advanced safety support system.”</p>\n<p>The 2019 investment into the Uber ATG unit deepened Toyota’s relationship with the company.</p>\n<p>&#8220;While Uber was facing off against Waymo in the trade secrets lawsuit, Aurora launched with a bang. Within 18 months, Auora had secured several kinds of partnerships with Hyundai, Byton and VW Group. Some have fizzled, while there have been new gains, notably with Fiat Chrysler Automobiles. The musical chair-like changes underscores the sheer number of hopeful players in the self-driving business &#8212; a market that is still full of commercial and technical unknowns &#8212; and the fickleness of incumbent car makers in search of the best tech and deal.&#8221;</p>\n<p>VW Group, which had touted its Aurora partnership in January 2018, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/11/vws-partnership-with-self-driving-car-startup-aurora-has-ended/\">confirmed to TechCrunch</a> in June 2019 that “activities under our partnership have been concluded.” VW Group ultimately put its capital behind Argo AI, another autonomous vehicle technology developer that had locked up backing and a customer deal with Ford.</p>\n<p>While Hyundai does have a minority stake in Aurora, it also went ahead and locked in a joint venture in fall 2019 with autonomous driving technology company Aptiv. Under the deal with Aptiv, both parties took a 50% ownership stake in the new joint company that is now called Motional. The combined investment in Motional from both companies will total $4 billion in aggregate value (including the value of combined engineering services, R&#38;D and IP).</p>\n<p>Still, Aurora has had its wins. The company raised $530 million last spring in a Series B round led by Sequoia with &#8220;significant investment&#8221; from Amazon and T. Rowe Price. Aurora&#8217;s post-money valuation at the time was $2.5 billion. More recently, sources <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">in the industry say that Aurora is abuzz with activity, particularly around the office of David Maday, the company&#8217;s new vice president of business development who led General Motors&#8217; corporate development and mergers and acquisitions team for 21 years.<br />\n</span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"FThlxtHsoq\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/02/07/amazon-sequoia-invest-in-self-driving-car-startup-aurora/\">Amazon, Sequoia invest in self-driving car startup Aurora</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Amazon, Sequoia invest in self-driving car startup Aurora&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/02/07/amazon-sequoia-invest-in-self-driving-car-startup-aurora/embed/#?secret=FThlxtHsoq\" data-secret=\"FThlxtHsoq\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Aurora has always stated that its full driving stack — the combined suite of software and hardware that provides the brains for an AV — would be vehicle-agnostic, but some of its early testing and partnerships suggested it was focused on robotaxi applications, not logistics. Aurora started talking more openly last year about applying its technology to long-haul trucking and has become more bullish on that application, particularly following its Blackmore acquisition.</p>\n<p>Aurora announced in July 2020 that it was expanding into Texas and planned to test commercial routes in the Dallas-Fort Worth Area with a mix of Fiat Chrysler Pacifica minivans and Class 8 trucks. A small fleet of Pacificas were expected to arrive first. The trucks will be on the road in Texas by the end of the year, according to the company.</p>\n<h2>The Jump precedent</h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What’s unclear is how an acquisition of Uber ATG might be structured; and more importantly, if it will retain any interest in the enterprise. Even with the expected depletion in Uber ATG’s valuation, it would be seemingly out-of-range for Aurora unless it was able to secure additional outside investment or structure the deal in a way that would allow Uber to keep some equity. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There is precedent for the latter. Earlier this year, Uber led a $170 million investment round into Lime. As part of the complex arrangement, Uber offloaded Jump, the bike and scooter-sharing unit, to Lime. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Rumors that Uber CEO Dara Khosrowshahi was keen to get rid of Uber ATG have popped up from time to time in the past year. But as the COVID-19 pandemic took hold, Khosrowshahi and other executives began to focus on its core competency of ride-hailing and double down on delivery. In addition to its micromobility unit and the Uber Freight spin-off, it has divested itself internationally of a number of regional operations that were proving too costly to grow in competition with strong local rivals.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It was on the heels of the Jump deal that interest in selling off Uber ATG ramped up, according to two sources.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One investor in the industry described it as an interesting Plan B for Uber, a deal that would allow the company to take ATG off the books, while potentially getting to benefit from a little upside.</span></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=F-7iN5MzV40:SQmzM-4_yDs:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img Korosec","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn57@2020_5/2020/11/15/06-18-39-312_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn15@2020_1/2020/11/15/06-19-06-004_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn10@2020_3/2020/11/15/06-19-03-843_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=F-7iN5MzV40:SQmzM-4_yDs:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn67@2020_3/2020/11/15/06-19-06-123_4ce014f9aaeadbae.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=F-7iN5MzV40:SQmzM-4_yDs:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn50@2020_3/2020/11/15/06-19-07-241_135ce8ea5bfc5ff9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn52@2020_4/2020/11/15/06-19-06-130_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/F-7iN5MzV40":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn46@2020_6/2020/11/15/06-19-03-908_472346a985302f42.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605421118977},{"createdTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"NextView Ventures closes its fourth fund with $89 million","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073991","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/nextview-ventures\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"nextview-ventures\">NextView Ventures, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> a Boston-based venture capital fund, has raised an $89.6 million fund, according to <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1799458/000179945820000002/xslFormDX01/primary_doc.xml\">SEC filings. </a>The firm’s fourth fund, its largest to date, is oversubscribed, with <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1799458/000179945820000001/xslFormDX01/primary_doc.xml\">early documents indicating</a> a $70 million goal. The NextView Ventures team did not immediately respond to request for comment.</p>\n<p>NextView Ventures was launched in 2010 by <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/robgo\">Rob Go</a>, a former partner at Spark Capital; <a href=\"https://nextviewventures.com/team/david-beisel/\">Dave Beisel</a>, who clocked time at Venrock and Masthead Venture Partners; and Lee Hower, a former investor at Point Judith Capital. Melody Koh joined as a partner three years ago, and most recently, the fund brought on former journalist <a href=\"https://twitter.com/LeahFessler\">Leah Fessler</a> as an investor.</p>\n<p>The fund, which has offices in New York as well as Boston, invests in consumer and software-as-a-service enterprise startups at the pre-seed and seed stage. Its portfolio includes <a href=\"https://www.ellevest.com/\">Ellevest</a>, an investing platform for women; <a href=\"https://www.grove.co/home\">Grove Collaborative</a>, a sustainable goods subscription platform; and ThredUp, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-thredup-ipo/goldman-sachs-backed-thredup-files-confidentially-for-ipo-idUSKBN2761YP\">which has confidentially filed for IPO</a>. In April, NextView launched a virtual <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/20/nextview-ventures-is-launching-a-remote-accelerator-for-startups/\">accelerator for startups </a>to build a more robust pipeline for deal flow. The firm invested $200,000 for an 8% equity stake in a number of pre-seed and seed startups focused on “<a href=\"https://nextviewventures.com/the-everyday-economy-accelerator/\">the everyday economy.</a>”</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--callout block--right\" >\n\t\t<h4 class=\"block--callout__title\">More Boston coverage</h4>\n\t\t\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/31/what-pandemic-inside-bostons-scorching-vc-summer/\">A hot Boston VC Summer</a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/18/13-boston-focused-investors-explain-present-life-in-the-startup-hub/\">13 Boston investors reflect on COVID-19</a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/08/as-funding-slows-in-boston-its-early-stage-market-could-shine/\">Local accelerators provide a boon to area startups</a></p>\n\t</div>\n\t</p>\n<p>Despite the pandemic, Boston’s startup scene has continued to attract <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/31/what-pandemic-inside-bostons-scorching-vc-summer/\">record numbers</a> in venture capital volume. In fact, according to PitchBook data, Boston-area startups raised more private capital during summer 2020 than they did in summer 2019, suggesting that the pandemic has been a boon to startups in aggregate.</p>\n<p>More recently, my colleague Alex Wilhelm and I wrote about<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/23/boston-startups-expand-regions-venture-capital-footprint/\"> how the Boston area is growing its demographic footprint in venture capital.</a> In Q3 2019, New England drove 9.3% of U.S. venture deals, and 10.3% of U.S. venture dollars. In Q3 2020, those numbers were 9.3% of U.S. venture deals, and 12.7% of U.S. venture dollars. The percentage change is notable, especially amid volatile times.</p>\n<p>NextView’s new fund is yet another signal of the city’s ability to attract institutional investment. Its previous fund was raised in 2017 <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/08/02/nextview-ventures-just-sealed-up-its-third-fund-with-50-million/\">at a $50 million close.</a></p>\n<div id=\"speakable-summary\">The venture capital market appears to be getting later, larger and more expensive. As a result, fintech — one of its hottest and most-funded sectors — is evolving in a similar manner.</p>\n<p>For late-stage fintech companies, it&#8217;s great news. But for smaller players, is the shift toward bigger, more mature rounds undercutting their ability to attract capital and reach scale?</p>\n<hr />\n<p><strong><em>The Exchange explores startups, markets and money. Read it <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/subscribe/?tpcc=theexchange\">every morning on Extra Crunch</a>, or get <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">The Exchange newsletter</a> every Saturday.</em></strong></p>\n<hr />\n<p>Venture capital getting later and larger was something we saw repeatedly in our examinations of what happened in Q3 2020 more broadly. For example, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/22/how-unicorns-helped-venture-capital-get-later-and-bigger/\">during our look into United States&#8217; results</a> during the period, we noted that &#8220;54% of all venture capital money invested in the United States in the third quarter was part of rounds that were $100 million or more,&#8221; with those 88 rounds &#8212; a record &#8212; totaling $19.8 billion.</p>\n<p>The other 1,373 rounds in the quarter had to split the rest of the money. And the percentage of rounds that are late-stage is rising, along with their average deal size, to add to the trend.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"skH1SYTaqg\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/19/late-stage-deals-made-q3-2020-a-standout-vc-quarter-for-us-based-startups/\">Late-stage deals made Q3 2020 a standout VC sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></a>This morning, leaning on <a href=\"https://pitchbook.com/news/reports/q3-2020-emerging-tech-research-fintech\">a report from PitchBook</a> covering fintech&#8217;s third quarter, I want to highlight how the vertical is also tilting later-stage &#8212; a trend to keep in mind as we care not only about which startups are gearing up to go public, but also which ones have a shot at raising the capital they need to make it to the growth stage.</p>\n<h2>More big, and more late</h2>\n<p>Top-line numbers from PitchBook concerning North American and European venture capital results for fintech in Q3 are as follows: $8.9 billion in total capital raised, +$1.3 billion or +17% from Q2 2020&#8217;s $7.6 billion haul.</p>\n<p>But, as PitchBook notes, &#8220;only 414 deals closed during the quarter—the lowest count since Q3 2017.&#8221; More capital then, into fewer rounds. That sounds familiar.</p>\n<p>Initially, when looking at the data set, we were going to note that consumer fintech startups are having a great year, while it appears that certain B2B fintech categories were pulling back. Indeed, after raising $3.7 billion in 2019, consumer-facing fintechs in North America and Europe have already raised $5.9 billion in 2020.</p>\n<p>But that growth story was dwarfed by the figures on this chart:</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073703\" style=\"width: 563px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073703\" loading=\"lazy\" 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"Online learning marketplace Udemy is raising up to $100M at a $3.32B valuation","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073814","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Online education has been one of the hotspots in the tech world this year, as people turn to e-learning tools to fill in the gaps variously arising from closed schools, closed offices, social distancing and more time on our hands at home because of the COVID-19 pandemic. And that is giving a big bump to education startups, which are raising money to capitalise on the growth opportunity.</p>\n<p>In one of the latest developments, <a href=\"http://udemy.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Udemy</a> &#8212; which provides a marketplace currently numbering some 130,000 video-based courses across 65 languages, ranging from learning Python or how to photograph better, through to mastering mindfulness and business analytics &#8212; is raising up to $100 million in a Series F round of funding that would value the company at up to $3.32 billion.</p>\n<p>The company has filed paperwork for the fundraise in Delaware, first discovered by Justin Byers and the team at <a href=\"https://primeunicornindex.com/udemy-secures-100m-series-f-round/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Prime Unicorn Index</a>. It&#8217;s not clear if the round has closed, and whether the full amount was raised (or indeed, more).</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Contacted for a response, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/udemy\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"udemy\">Udemy <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> didn&#8217;t deny the report but also declined to say anything for the moment. &#8220;We have a company policy where we don’t comment on speculations,&#8221; a spokesperson said to me via email. &#8220;We don’t have a comment at this time but I’ll reach out if anything changes.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The fundraise would be a strong move for Udemy, which only closed its Series E earlier this year &#8212; a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/02/19/online-learning-marketplace-udemy-raises-50m-at-a-2b-valuation-from-japanese-publisher-benesse/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">$50 million round</a> that catapulted the company to a $2 billion+ post-money valuation.</p>\n<p>But that was in February, before the novel coronavirus really took hold of the world. Since then, startups focused on education have been seeing a surge of business starting in the spring of this year, and as a result, also a surge of attention from investors who see a good moment to back rising stars.</p>\n<p>Just looking at some of the most recent deals, last week, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/03/udacity-raises-75m-in-debt-says-its-tech-education-business-is-profitable-after-enterprise-pivot/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Udacity </a>announced a $75 million debt round and said it was finally profitable. In October, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/kahoot-picks-up-215m-from-softbank-for-its-user-generated-gamified-e-learning-platform/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Kahoot</a> announced a $215 million round from SoftBank. And in September, Outschool <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/18/outschool-newly-profitable-raises-a-45m-series-b-for-virtual-small-group-classes/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">raised $45 million</a> (and is now profitable); Homer <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/30/homer-nabs-50m-from-lego-sesame-workshop-and-gymboree-for-its-early-learning-apps/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">raised $50 million</a> (from an impressive group of strategic backers); Unacademy <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/02/indias-online-learning-platform-unacademy-raises-150-million-at-1-45-billion-valuation/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">raised $150 million</a> and the juggernaut that is Byju’s picked up <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/07/silver-lake-leads-500-million-round-in-indias-byjus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">$500 million from Silver Lake</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"JtRJ02KyqH\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/02/indias-online-learning-platform-unacademy-raises-150-million-at-1-45-billion-valuation/\">India&#8217;s online learning platform Unacademy raises $150 million at $1.45 billion valuation</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;India&#8217;s online learning platform Unacademy raises $150 million at $1.45 billion valuation&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/02/indias-online-learning-platform-unacademy-raises-150-million-at-1-45-billion-valuation/embed/#?secret=JtRJ02KyqH\" data-secret=\"JtRJ02KyqH\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>And these are just some of the bigger deals; there have been many <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/nana-nabs-6m-for-an-online-academy-and-marketplace-dedicated-to-appliance-repair/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">smaller fundraises</a>, new <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/engageli-comes-out-of-stealth-with-14-5m-and-a-new-approach-to-teaching-by-video-remotely/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">edtech startup launches</a> and other <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/11/vcs-pour-funding-into-edtech-startups-as-covid-19-shakes-up-the-market/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">signs of momentum</a> alongside <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/09/edtech-startups-prepare-to-become-not-just-a-teaching-tool-but-a-necessity/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">this</a>. (And Prime Unicorn, incidentally, also noted that <a href=\"https://primeunicornindex.com/duolingo-secures-35m-series-h-round/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Duolingo</a> is also raising money, up to $35 million at a valuation of $2.21 billion if all shares are issued. We&#8217;re still digging on that lead.)</p>\n<p>When Udemy last raised money, earlier this year, the president of the business division told me it had clocked up 50 million students that purchase courses in an à la carte format, while enterprise customers &#8212; which include Adidas, General Mills, Toyota, Wipro, Pinterest and Lyft in a list of some 5,000 in all &#8212; use a subscription model.</p>\n<p>It looks like its business users have grown and now number over 7,000, according to <a href=\"https://about.udemy.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">figures</a> on its site, with total course enrollments now totalling 400 million to date. That could point to the opportunity that Udemy is now exploring with more capital.</p>\n<p>But to be clear, the filing does not detail who is in this latest round, nor what the purpose of the fundraising is.</p>\n<p>As we wrote at the time of the round in February, that fundraise came from a single, strategic investor, the Japanese educational publisher Benesse Holdings, which partners with Udemy in Japan. Benesse&#8217;s bigger business includes developing educational content for children and courses for adults, both online and in-person, and for other educational brands that it owns, such as <a href=\"http://berlitz.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Berlitz</a>, and Udemy helps Benesse develop content for those various efforts.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"0nqXJMIpoo\"><p><a business is profitable after enterprise pivot</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Udacity raises $75M in 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"Demon’s Souls: The first truly next-gen game is a lopsided but impressive showcase","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073801","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The next generation of gaming is here with the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/06/review-sonys-playstation-5-is-here-but-next-generation-gaming-is-still-on-its-way/\">PlayStation 5</a> and Xbox Series X — except it isn&#8217;t, because there are almost no next-generation games to play on them. <em>Demon&#8217;s Souls</em> is the first title that can truly be called next-gen, and it shows — even though it&#8217;s a remake of a PS3 game&#8230; which also shows.</p>\n<p>The original <em>Demon&#8217;s Souls</em> was an incredibly influential game. Its sequel, <em>Dark Souls</em>, was more popular and improved on the first quite a bit, but much of what made the now major series good had already been established. &#8220;Souls-like&#8221; is practically a genre now, though the originals are unsurprisingly still the <em>nonpareil</em>.</p>\n<p>The comparative few who played <em>Demon&#8217;s Souls</em> were elated to hear that it was being remade, and by Bluepoint at that (who also remade the legendary <em>Shadow of the Colossus</em>), but worried that the game might not stand up by modern standards.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Can an old game, the essentials of which are a decade behind its descendants, be given a really, really, really <em>ridiculously</em> good-looking coat of paint and still act as a blockbuster next-gen debut? Well, it kind of has to — there&#8217;s no other option! Fortunately the game really does hold up, and in fact makes for a harrowing, cinematic experience despite a few significant creaks.</p>\n<p>I don&#8217;t want to give a full review of the game itself; let it suffice to say that, although it looks and runs much better, the core of the game is almost entirely unchanged. Any review from the last decade is still completely relevant, down to the &#8220;magic is overpowered&#8221; and &#8220;inventory burden is annoying.&#8221;</p>\n<p>As a next-gen gaming experience, however, <em>Demon&#8217;s Souls</em> is as yet without comparison. It serves as a showcase not only for the PS5&#8217;s graphical prowess, but its sound design, haptics, speed and OS.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073893\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073893\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2073893\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg 2500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-3.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2073893\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Sony</p></div></p>\n<p>First, the graphics. It&#8217;s clear that Sony and Bluepoint intended this to be a truly lavish remake, and the game&#8217;s structure — essentially five long, mostly linear levels — provides an excellent platform for breathtaking visuals carefully tuned to the user&#8217;s experience.</p>\n<p>The environments themselves are incredibly detailed, and the various enemies you fight very well realized, but what I kept being impressed by was the lighting. Realistic lighting is something that has proven difficult even for top-tier developers, and it&#8217;s only now that the hardware has enough headroom to start doing it properly.</p>\n<p><em>Demon&#8217;s Souls</em> doesn&#8217;t use ray-tracing, the computation-heavy lighting technique perennially on the cusp of being implemented, but the real-time lighting effects are nevertheless dramatic and extremely engaging. This is a dark, dark world and the player is very limited as far as personal light sources, meaning the way you experience the environment is carefully designed.</p>\n<p>Although the detailed armor, props and monsters are all very nice, it&#8217;s the realistic lighting that really sets them off in a way that seems truly new and beautiful. Dynamic range is used properly, to have actually dark areas illuminated dramatically, such as the still-terrifying Tower of Latria.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073891\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073891\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2073891\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg 2500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/demons-souls-1.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2073891\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Sony</p></div></p>\n<p>The game isn&#8217;t a huge leap over the best the PC has to offer right now, but it does make me excited for game designers who really want to use light and shadow as gameplay elements.</p>\n<p>(Incidentally, don&#8217;t bother with the &#8220;cinematic&#8221; option versus &#8220;performance.&#8221; The latter keeps the game silky smooth, which for <em>Souls</em> games is a luxury, and the other setting didn&#8217;t improve the look much if at all, while severely affecting the framerate. Skip it unless you&#8217;re taking glamour shots.)</p>\n<p>Similarly sound is extremely well done in the game, though I&#8217;m cautious about hyping Sony&#8217;s &#8220;3D audio&#8221; — really, games have had this sort of thing for years on many platforms. Having a decent pair of headphones is the important bit. But perhaps the PS5 offers improved workflows for spatializing sound; at all events in <em>Demon&#8217;s Souls</em> it was very good, with great separation, location and clarity. I have reliably dodged an enemy attack from offscreen after recognizing the characteristic grunt of an attacking foe, and the screeches and roars of dragons and boss monsters (as well as the general <em>milieu</em> of Latria) were suitably chilling.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2065845\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2065845\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2065845\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg\" alt=\"A Sony DualSense controller seen from above.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"659\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg 2500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=150,97 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=300,193 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=768,494 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=680,438 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=1536,989 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=2048,1318 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2065845\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Sony</p></div></p>\n<p>This combined well with the improved haptics of the DualSense controller, which seemed to have a different &#8220;sensation&#8221; for every event. A dragon flying overhead, a demon stomping the ground, a blocked attack, an elevator ride. Mostly these were good and only aided immersion, but some, like the elevators, felt to me more like an annoying buzz than a rumble, like holding a power tool. I hope that developers will be sensible about these things and identify vibration patterns that are irritating. Fortunately the intensity can be adjusted universally in the PS5&#8217;s controls.</p>\n<p>Likewise the adaptive triggers were nice but not game-changing. It was helpful when using the bow to know when the arrow was ready to release, for instance, but beyond a few things like that it was not used to great advantage.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"rIdDU3bA6C\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/27/hands-on-sonys-dualsense-ps5-controller-could-be-a-game-changer/\">Hands-on: Sony&#8217;s DualSense PS5 controller could be a game changer</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Hands-on: Sony&#8217;s DualSense PS5 controller could be a game changer&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/27/hands-on-sonys-dualsense-ps5-controller-could-be-a-game-changer/embed/#?secret=rIdDU3bA6C\" data-secret=\"rIdDU3bA6C\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Something that had a more immediate effect on how I played was the incredibly short load times. The Souls series has always been plagued by long load times when traveling and dying, the latter of which you can expect to do a lot. But now it&#8217;s rare that I can count to three before I&#8217;m materializing at the bonfire again.</p>\n<p>This significantly reduces (but far from eliminates) frustration in this infamously unforgiving game, and actually makes me play it differently. Where once I could not be bothered to briefly travel to another area or the hub in order to accomplish some small task, now I know I can return to the Nexus, fuss around a bit with my loadout and be back in Boletaria in 30 seconds flat. If I die, I&#8217;m back in action in five seconds rather than 20, and believe me, that adds up real fast. (Load times are improved across the board in PS4 games running on the PS5 as well.)</p>\n<p>Aiding this, kind of, is the new fancy pause screen Sony has implemented on its new console. When hitting the (annoyingly PS-shaped) PS button, a set of &#8220;cards&#8221; appears showing recent achievements and screenshots, but also ongoing missions or game progress. Pausing in Latria to take a breath, the menu offered up the ability to instantly warp to one of the other worlds, losing my souls but skipping the ordinarily requisite Nexus stop. This will certainly change how speedruns are accomplished, and provides a useful, if somewhat immersion-breaking option for the scatterbrained player.</p>\n<p>The pause menu also provides a venue for tips and hints, in both text and video form. Again, this is a funny game to debut these in (I don&#8217;t count <em>Astro&#8217;s Playroom</em>, the included game/tech demo, which is fun but slight), because one of the <em>Souls</em> series&#8217;s distinctive features is player-generated notes and ghosts that alternatively warn and deceive new players. In another game I might have relied on the PS5&#8217;s hints more, but for this specific title they seem somewhat redundant.</p>\n<p>As arguably the only &#8220;real&#8221; PS5 launch title, <em>Demon&#8217;s Souls</em> is a curious but impressive creature. It definitely shows the new console to advantage in some ways, but the game itself (while still amazing) is dated in many ways, limiting the possibilities of what can be shown off in the first place.</p>\n<p>Certainly the remake is the best (and for many, only) way to play a classic, and for that alone it is recommended — though the $70 price (more in Europe and elsewhere) is definitely a bit of a squinter. One would hope that for the new higher asking price, we could expect next-generation gameplay as well as next-generation trimmings. Well, for now we have to take what we can get.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"fLrywlT6mh\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/06/review-sonys-playstation-5-is-here-but-next-generation-gaming-is-still-on-its-way/\">Review: Sony&#8217;s PlayStation 5 is here, but next-generation gaming is still on its way</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Review: Sony&#8217;s PlayStation 5 is here, but
