14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"Which emerging technologies are enterprise companies getting serious about in 2020?","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073435","description":"<div class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-name\">Scott Kirsner</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-title\" style=\"display: block;\">Contributor</span>\n\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"contributor__twitter\">\n\t\t\t<a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://twitter.com/ScottKirsner\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<svg class=\"icon icon--twitter icon--white\" viewBox=\"0 0 20 20\" version=\"1.1\" aria-labelledby=\"title\">\n\t\t<title>Share on Twitter</title>\n\t\t<path d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"/>\t</svg>\n\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tScott Kirsner is CEO and co-founder of <a href=\"https://www.innovationleader.com/\">Innovation Leader</a>, a research and events firm that focuses on innovation in Global 1000 companies, and a longtime business columnist for The Boston Globe.\n\t</div>\n\t\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">Startups need to live in the future. They create roadmaps, build products and continually upgrade them with an eye on next year — or even a few years out.</p>\n<p>Big companies, often the target customers for startups, live in a much more near-term world. They buy technologies that can solve problems they know about today, rather than those they may face a couple bends down the road. In other words, they’re driving a Dodge, and most tech entrepreneurs are driving a DeLorean equipped with a flux-capacitor.</p>\n<p>That situation can lead to a huge waste of time for startups that want to sell to enterprise customers: a business development black hole. Startups are talking about technology shifts and customer demands that the executives inside the large company — even if they have “innovation,” “IT,” or “emerging technology” in their titles — just don’t see as an urgent priority yet, or can’t sell to their colleagues.</p>\n<p>How do you avoid the aforementioned black hole? Some recent research that my company, <a href=\"https://www.innovationleader.com/\">Innovation Leader</a>, conducted in collaboration with <a href=\"https://home.kpmg/xx/en/home.html\">KPMG LLP</a>, suggests a constructive approach.</p>\n<p>Rather than asking large companies about which technologies they were experimenting with, we created four buckets, based on what you might call “commitment level.” (Our survey had 211 respondents, 62% of them in North America and 59% at companies with greater than $1 billion in annual revenue.) We asked survey respondents to assess a list of 16 technologies, from advanced analytics to quantum computing, and put each one into one of these four buckets. We conducted the survey at the tail end of Q3 2020.</p>\n<p>Respondents in the first group were &#8220;not exploring or investing&#8221; — in other words, &#8220;we don’t care about this right now.&#8221; The top technology there was quantum computing.</p>\n<p>Bucket #2 was the second-lowest commitment level: &#8220;learning and exploring.&#8221; At this stage, a startup gets to educate its prospective corporate customer about an emerging technology — but nabbing a purchase commitment is still quite a few exits down the highway. It can be constructive to begin building relationships when a company is at this stage, but your sales staff shouldn’t start calculating their commissions just yet.</p>\n<p>Here are the top five things that fell into the “learning and exploring&#8221; cohort, in ranked order:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Blockchain.</li>\n<li>Augmented reality/mixed reality.</li>\n<li>Virtual reality.</li>\n<li>AI/machine learning.</li>\n<li>Wearable devices.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Technologies in the third group, &#8220;investing or piloting,&#8221; may represent the sweet spot for startups. At this stage, the corporate customer has already discovered some internal problem or use case that the technology might address. They may have shaken loose some early funding. They may have departments internally, or test sites externally, where they know they can conduct pilots. Often, they’re assessing what established tech vendors like <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/microsoft\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"microsoft\">Microsoft, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/oracle\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"oracle\">Oracle <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Cisco can provide — and they may find their solutions wanting.</p>\n<p>Here’s what our survey respondents put into the &#8220;investing or piloting&#8221; bucket, in ranked order:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Advanced analytics.</li>\n<li>AI/machine learning.</li>\n<li>Collaboration tools and software.</li>\n<li>Cloud infrastructure and services.</li>\n<li>Internet of things/new sensors.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>By the time a technology is placed into the fourth category, which we dubbed &#8220;in-market or accelerating investment,&#8221; it may be too late for a startup to find a foothold. There’s already a clear understanding of at least <em>some</em> of the use cases or problems that need solving, and return-on-investment metrics have been established. But some providers have already been chosen, based on successful pilots and you may need to dislodge someone that the enterprise is already working with. It can happen, but the headwinds are strong.</p>\n<p>Here’s what the survey respondents placed into the &#8220;in-market or accelerating investment&#8221; bucket, in ranked order:<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=ff8dzt7GrZc:VCUfJZlE6sE:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=ff8dzt7GrZc:VCUfJZlE6sE:7Q72WNTAKBA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=ff8dzt7GrZc:VCUfJZlE6sE:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=ff8dzt7GrZc:VCUfJZlE6sE:-BTjWOF_DHI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=ff8dzt7GrZc:VCUfJZlE6sE:-BTjWOF_DHI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a href=\"https://9to5google.com/2020/11/13/google-expeditions/\">today announced</a> that it is ending support for Expeditions. The VR app will also be pulled from its own Play Store and Apple’s App Store in June of next year. In a blogpost <a href=\"https://blog.google/outreach-initiatives/education/expanding-google-arts-and-culture-expeditions#:~:text=That%20spirit%20of%20possibility%20also,about%20cultures%20unlike%20their%20own.\">somewhat confusingly titled</a>, “Expanding Google Arts and Culture with Expeditions,” the company notes the 360-degree tours captured for the project will survive — but will be moved to Google Arts &#38; Culture.</p>\n<p>Director of Program Management, Education, Jennifer Holland, says the decision was made to make the content more accessible to students and educators.</p>\n<p>“Engaging students in the classroom has taken on an entirely different meaning this year. As schools around the world reimagine education from the ground up for a hybrid world, we’ve also been thinking deeply about how to adjust our tools to meet the moment and simultaneously build for the future,” she writes. “We’ve heard and recognize that immersive experiences with VR headsets are not always accessible to all learners and even more so this year, as the transition to hybrid learning has presented challenges for schools to effectively use Expeditions.”</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-2073977\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GAC_Expeditions_1.max-1000x1000-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"650\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GAC_Expeditions_1.max-1000x1000-1.png 1000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GAC_Expeditions_1.max-1000x1000-1.png?resize=150,98 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GAC_Expeditions_1.max-1000x1000-1.png?resize=300,195 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GAC_Expeditions_1.max-1000x1000-1.png?resize=768,499 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GAC_Expeditions_1.max-1000x1000-1.png?resize=680,442 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GAC_Expeditions_1.max-1000x1000-1.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></p>\n<p>The content will be included alongside Arts &#38; Culture’s museum tours and other content, available for free to all users. That, at least, is a small win for teachers and parents who have struggled to keep up kids&#8217; education in the face of a pandemic that has contributed to major school closures.</p>\n<p>Notably, the news comes a little over a month after Google announced it would be ending support for the ill-fated <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/daydream-42c8\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"daydream-42c8\">Daydream <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> VR platform. 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"How COVID-19 accelerated DoorDash’s business","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073810","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/doordash\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"doordash\">DoorDash <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> filed to go public today, publishing numbers that <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/doordash-files-to-go-public/\">showed rapid growth</a>, enhanced profitability and an improving cash flow record which helped explain how the company had grown to a $16 billion valuation while private. The unicorn&#8217;s impending liquidity event will <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/the-vc-and-founder-winners-of-doordashs-ipo/\">enrich a host of venture capital firms</a> that bet on its eventual maturity.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><i>Instead of posting this entry of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/the-exchange/\">The Exchange</a> on Monday, we&#8217;ve put it out today for your Friday and weekend reading. Enjoy! &#8212; <a href=\"https://twitter.com/alex\">Alex</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/yourprotagonist\">Walter</a>. </i></p>\n<hr />\n<p>But notable in DoorDash&#8217;s impressive results is the impact of COVID-19, accelerating secular trends already in place, and boosting the unicorn&#8217;s growth. Before we get into pricing this IPO and guessing what the company might be worth, let&#8217;s strive to understand what portion of its 2020 business gains could stem from the pandemic — and might not persist into the future.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;re not being pessimistic; we merely want to better understand the company. And DoorDash agrees with our general thrust, writing in its S-1 filing that &#8220;58% of all adults and 70% of millennials say that they are more likely to have restaurant food delivered than they were two years ago,&#8221; adding that it believes &#8220;the COVID-19 pandemic has further accelerated these trends.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Even more, elsewhere in its filings DoorDash states plainly that COVD-19 led it to experience &#8220;a significant increase in revenue, Total Orders, and Marketplace [gross order volume] due to increased consumer demand for delivery, more merchants using our platform to facilitate both delivery and take-out, and improved efficiency of our local logistics platform.&#8221; The company then went on to warn investors that the &#8220;circumstances that have accelerated the growth of our business stemming from the effects of the COVID-19 pandemic may not continue in the future, and we expect the growth rates in revenue, Total Orders, and Marketplace [gross order volume] to decline in future periods.&#8221;</p>\n<p>We&#8217;re not idly speculating.</p>\n<p>Let&#8217;s observe how DoorDash&#8217;s growth accelerated from 2019 through 2020 and then peek at how the company&#8217;s economics improved during the same period, giving the company a shot at adjusted profitability for the full year, a nearly unheard of result in the on-demand market.</p>\n<h2>Growth</h2>\n<p>DoorDash generates revenue when a customer orders food via its service, splitting the total bill of food costs, taxes, fees and tips, distributing them to itself, the merchant creating the goods and the delivery person.</p>\n<p>In an &#8220;illustrative&#8221; example that DoorDash notes its 2019 &#8220;approximate average per-order information,&#8221; the split works out as follows:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Bill:</strong> $32.90</li>\n<li><strong>Merchant:</strong> $20.10, or 61%</li>\n<li><strong>DoorDash:</strong> $4.90, or 15%</li>\n<li><strong>Delivery person:</strong> $7.90, or 24%</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Given that the company is giving us old data and DoorDash&#8217;s performance has been stellar this year in terms of generating more gross profit, I wonder what has happened amidst 2020&#8217;s upheaval. But, the old numbers do for what we need, which is to understand the link between gross order volume (GOV) and DoorDash revenue. When the former goes up, the latter goes up.</p>\n<p>So, as orders rise:</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-2073816\" 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"Getaround tops up $25M debt financing to its $140M Series E","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073755","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Silicon Valley peer-to-peer car rental startup <a href=\"https://www.getaround.com/\">Getaround</a> has secured <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/horizon-technology-finance-provides-25-million-venture-loan-facility-to-getaround-301172251.html\">a $25 million loan</a> from Horizon Technology Finance Corporation. The financing announcement comes one month after Getaround raised <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/getaround-raises-a-140-million-series-e-amid-rebound-in-short-distance-travel/\">$140 million</a> from investors, including SoftBank Vision Fund, Menlo Ventures, Reid Hoffman and Mark Pincus’ Reinvent Capital.</span></p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/getaround\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"getaround\">Getaround’s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> raise signals that the company is looking for new ways to secure cash without further diluting executives or investors.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">A Getaround spokesperson said “Horizon presented an opportunity that provides us with additional capital to accelerate our plans in the same way as our recent Series E fundraise.”</span></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><a href=\"https://horizontechfinance.com/team/leadership/daniel-s-devorsetz/\">Dan Devorsetz</a>, Horizon’s chief investment officer, told TechCrunch that venture debt has been a part of Getaround’s financing strategy for 2020.</p>\n<p>“It diversifies funding sources and lowers their overall cost of capital, while also mitigating the dilution impact of incremental equity,” he said. While he wouldn’t clarify on where the debt capital was going, he said that the debt is allowing Getaround to accomplish both “working capital needs and long-term strategic growth initiatives.”</p>\n<p>Getaround, like many travel-related startups, struggled in the beginning of the pandemic as governments issued stay-at-home orders in an effort to keep the disease caused by coronavirus from spreading. Bookings dropped 75% in March, forcing Getaround to lay off 100 employees. The company also applied and received approval for a Paycheck Protection Program loan to help retain workers. Getaround previously told TechCrunch that the program “helped reduce the otherwise severe impact on the health of our organization,” due to lockdowns and coronavirus restrictions.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ZUVHdfbAyA\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/21/how-one-founder-leveraged-debt-to-drive-early-growth-and-avoid-dilution/\">How one founder leveraged debt to drive early growth and avoid dilution</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;How one founder leveraged debt to drive early growth and avoid dilution&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/21/how-one-founder-leveraged-debt-to-drive-early-growth-and-avoid-dilution/embed/#?secret=ZUVHdfbAyA\" data-secret=\"ZUVHdfbAyA\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Demand returned in May as travelers turned to cars instead of flights for short-distance trips. Getaround CEO <a href=\"https://twitter.com/samzaid\">Sam Zaid</a> last told TechCrunch that worldwide revenue has more than doubled from pre-COVID baselines.</p>\n<p>By July, Getaround said it had rehired all of its furloughed employees.</p>\n<p>There have been scattered signs of a comeback throughout the mobility industry. This week, Uber had <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/uber-has-its-highest-close-since-ipo/\">its highest close since IPO, </a>and Lyft saw its <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/lyft-sees-ride-revenues-recover-by-nearly-50-in-just-three-months/\">ride revenues recover enough</a> to give investors some calm.</p>\n<p>The upshot: The green shoots have sprouted. But will another wave of COVID-19 nip those buds before they can establish roots?</p>\n<p>Getaround&#8217;s decision to pursue debt financing so soon after raising a six-figure venture capital round could signal the company&#8217;s anticipation of another lockdown, and subsequent drop in bookings. Unlike other mobility companies, Getaround doesn&#8217;t own the cars, trucks and SUVs on its rental platform, a benefit that could help the company weather a short downturn.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"vzsJ2xT231\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/top-mobility-vcs-on-the-risks-and-rewards-in-partnering-with-giants-like-amazon/\">Top mobility VCs on the risks and rewards in partnering with giants like Amazon</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Top mobility VCs on the risks and rewards in partnering with 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"Nintendo’s Mario Game & Watch is a choice gaming stocking stuffer","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2071585","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/nintendo\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"nintendo\">Nintendo <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> will never stop mining its past for new nostalgia-based products, but at least it tends to do so with aplomb and occasionally even generosity. The former at least is on display with the <a href=\"https://gameandwatch.nintendo.com/\">Super Mario Bros. Game &#38; Watch</a>, a standalone handheld that plays the first Mario game, its unbelievably hard &#8220;Lost Levels&#8221; sequel and acts as a totally impractical timepiece.</p>\n<p>This tiny gaming system isn&#8217;t the most practical thing in the world, but it is a charming piece of hardware that does exactly what it says on the tin.</p>\n<p>Turn on the Game &#38; Watch with a button on the side and you can select between, naturally, the Game and Watch modes. In game mode, you can select between playing the original Super Mario Bros. for NES, the sequel we never got in the U.S., but was eventually released as &#8220;The Lost Levels,&#8221; and a recreation of an old-school LCD game where Mario juggles balls at ever-increasing speeds.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2072175\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2072175\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2072175\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg\" alt=\"Nintendo's Super Mario Bros handheld system\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg 2500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-2.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2072175\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Devin Coldewey / TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>The screen, while certainly small, is bright and sharp, apparently displaying the exact pixel dimensions of the original Nintendo game. It plays well, too — the controls are responsive, though it feels strange to play the game on anything other than an original NES controller. The buttons of the Game &#38; Watch are a bit softer than I&#8217;d like — but they were good enough that I cleared the first set of levels without any real frustration other than my own lack of skill.</p>\n<p>While there is no support for saving or rewinding the game — pretty much essential for the 99% of us who can&#8217;t beat it honestly — at least you don&#8217;t have to try to beat it in one sitting. The game freezes its state when you turn if off or switch to any other game or mode, meaning you can play a couple levels between subway stops and not worry about losing progress.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2072174\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-1.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2072174\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2072174\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-1.jpg\" alt=\"Nintendo's Super Mario Bros handheld system, side view\" width=\"1024\" height=\"727\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-1.jpg 2500w, 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-1.jpg?resize=768,545 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-1.jpg?resize=680,483 680w, 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2072174\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Devin Coldewey / TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>You can hand it back and forth with a friend (after sanitizing it, of course) too, since player 2 uses the same controls.</p>\n<p>The juggling game is a fun little diversion but, like most of those old LCD games, goes from really boring to nearly impossible in the course of about 60 seconds.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2072176\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2072176\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2072176\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg 2500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg?resize=150,104 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg?resize=300,208 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg?resize=768,533 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg?resize=680,472 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg?resize=1536,1066 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg?resize=2048,1421 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nintendo-game-watch-mario-3.jpg?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2072176\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Devin Coldewey / TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>The &#8220;Watch&#8221; mode has a charming little landscape with the current time made out of bricks, and Mario running across the screen below stomping goombas and avoiding Bullet Bills. If you watch for a while he&#8217;ll moonwalk, mount a pipe and perform other hijinks. You can switch the background from normal to hills to mushroom platforms. I wouldn&#8217;t use it as a watch, but if you don&#8217;t want to pull your phone out while you&#8217;re playing, there you go.</p>\n<p>For $50 it may seem a little steep, and perhaps it is. If this had Marios 1 through 3 on it I would consider it a bargain, especially considering the ability to come back to the game time after time — I&#8217;d work my way through the epic-length third game with pleasure.</p>\n<p>As it is, however, it&#8217;s hard to justify the price — except, of course, as a gift to a Nintendo-loving friend or loved one. That&#8217;s why I suspect these will sell like hotcakes this holiday season. With no new Switch hardware, no N64 mini and no must-have games on Nintendo&#8217;s platforms, it&#8217;s looking a bit dry, but a Game &#38; Watch is just silly enough — and decent enough — a device to sate the hunger of a retro-minded gamer for a few days.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"TbD3r67TPB\"><p><a 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"DoorDash IPO bets that the pandemic has accelerated change","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073984","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><strong>Editor’s note:<a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/bilal-zuberi\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"bilal-zuberi\"> </a></strong><em>Get this free weekly recap of TechCrunch news that any startup can use by email every Saturday morning (7 a.m. PT). <a href=\"http://link.techcrunch.com/join/134/signup-all-newsletters?_ga=2.28241148.139228165.1581112174-1679447956.1560885729\">Subscribe here</a>.</em></p>\n<p>DoorDash has become the go-to delivery choice for millions of people cooped up during the pandemic this year. Now it has filed an S-1, revealing its financials as it nears a long-intended IPO. These innards show an exciting business — and a larger story about how the year is going for tech companies in general.</p>\n<p>When the company filed initial public offering paperwork back in February, it was coming off of an expensive year of growth in 2019. The California state legislature was passing laws, meanwhile, that directly targeted its gig-economy labor model. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/doordash-files-to-go-public/\">Then the pandemic hit. More from Alex Wilhelm</a>:</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<blockquote><p>DoorDash has grown incredibly rapidly, scaling its revenues from $291 million in 2018 to $885 million in 2019. And more recently, from $587 million in the first nine months of 2019 to $1.92 billion in the same period of 2020. That is 226% growth in 2020 thus far&#8230; How high-quality is DoorDash’s revenue? In the first three quarters of 2019, the company had gross margins of 39.9%, and in the same period of 2020 the figure rose to 53.1%, a huge improvement for the consumer consumable delivery confab.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The other jolt of good news for the company arrived last week. A California ballot proposition passed that preserved the contractor model it relies on for deliveries.</p>\n<p>World events did not take a breath, though. A COVID-19 vaccine appeared on the horizon this week, and could lead to the pandemic ending as soon as next year. Will this be bad for DoorDash&#8217;s business? Alex took <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/how-covid-19-accelerated-doordashs-business/\">another look at the numbers for Extra Crunch</a>, and didn&#8217;t come away with a clear answer. On the one hand, the company has been making ongoing investments in its delivery platform technology, which has helped to drive the success this year already. On the other hand, the S-1 is open about post-pandemic reality — profitability is going to decline. Alex:</p>\n<blockquote><p>To buy into the DoorDash IPO, especially at its <a href=\"https://twitter.com/alex/status/1327313096587829248\">currently floated $25 billion price</a>, you have to believe that the company’s revenue <em>growth</em> will slow modestly at <em>most</em>. Otherwise the price makes no sense. Bearish investors who might expect the company to post negative growth in Q3 2021 won’t pay any price for DoorDash shares, but in between the two camps is a mess of vaccine timings, shifts in consumer behavior and macroeconomic questions that could determine how many American families can afford delivery. All of which will impact DoorDash’s future growth rates.</p></blockquote>\n<p>For those looking further out, DoorDash stock is about how you think the pandemic is going to change the world for the long term, or not. Are we going to be using DoorDash more often now for deliveries? Are we going to be at home as much in the first place? Or are we going to go back to offices, stores and restaurants like we did before?</p>\n<p>Speaking of investors, Danny Crichton illustrates why it pays to bet on the world changing. The company has raised nearly $2.5 billion over the years. Today that includes an 18.2% ownership stake by Sequoia, 22.1% by the SoftBank Vision Fund, and 9.3% by Singapore&#8217;s GIC. As he <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/the-vc-and-founder-winners-of-doordashs-ipo/\">writes for Extra Crunch</a>, the founding executives Tony Xu, Andy Fang and Stanley Tang each own around 5% — smallish wedges of a growing pie. Maybe that is too much dilution? Or maybe, considering all of the other delivery companies that have failed or gone sideways, this is the pinnacle of success in the sector.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2071234\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2071234\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2071234\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg\" alt=\"A health care worker holds an injection syringe of the phase 3 vaccine trial, developed against the novel coronavirus (COVID-19) pandemic by the U.S. Pfizer and German BioNTech company, at the Ankara University Ibni Sina Hospital in Ankara, Turkey\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg 2126w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg?resize=2048,1366 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1229305344.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2071234\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Photo by Dogukan Keskinkilic/Anadolu Agency via Getty Images)</p></div></p>\n<h2><em><strong>The Vaccine</strong></em></h2>\n<p>We all knew that at some point solutions would be figured out. But as COVID-19 cases have climbed this season, and as anxiety built around elections, it was hard to believe that <em>the vaccine</em> was right around the corner. The <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/pfizers-covid-19-vaccine-proves-90-effective-in-first-results-from-phase-3-clinical-trial/\">initial success reported Monday by BioNTech and Pfizer</a> may mean that these two companies are close to success. But many other companies are attempting to use the same experimental gene-based vaccines so we may see others winners soon.</p>\n<p>The stock market is already repricing tech stocks, in any case. Besides the timely arrival of the DoorDash S-1, here are a few other headlines about the impact of the news:</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/positive-vaccine-news-punishes-pandemic-boosted-companies-like-zoom-peloton-etsy/\">Positive vaccine news punishes pandemic-boosted companies like Zoom, Peloton, Etsy</a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/what-happens-to-high-flying-startups-if-the-pandemic-trade-flips/\">What happens to high-flying startups if the pandemic trade flips? (EC)</a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/5-vcs-discuss-the-future-of-saas-and-software-after-pfizers-vaccine-breakthrough/\">5 VCs discuss the future of SaaS and software after Pfizer’s vaccine breakthrough (EC)</a></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1458839\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1458839\" 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1458839\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> John Artman</p></div></p>\n<h2>Tencent&#8217;s fintech business is the size of an Ant</h2>\n<p>In other news about political turbulence and the tech world, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/tencent-vs-alibaba-ant-fintech/\">Rita Liao inspects Tencent&#8217;s quietly huge fintech empire</a> and concludes that it &#8220;will need to tread more carefully on regulatory issues.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s why, for those trying to understand this global company and its place across markets:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As Ant Group seizes the world’s attention with its <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/26/ant-group-could-raise-as-much-as-34-5b-in-ipo-in-what-would-be-worlds-largest-ipo/\">record</a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/20/alibaba-ant-ipo/\">initial public offering</a>, which was abruptly<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/03/china-postpones-ants-colossal-ipo-after-closed-door-talk-with-jack-ma/\"> called off by Beijing</a>, investors and analysts are revisiting the fintech interests of Tencent, Ant’s arch rival in China. It’s somewhat complicated to do this, not least because they are sprawled across a number of Tencent properties and, unlike Ant, don’t go by a single brand or operational structure — at least, not one that is obvious to the outside world. However, when you tease out Tencent’s fintech activity across its wider footprint — from direct operations like WeChat Pay through to its sizeable strategic investments and third-party marketplaces — you have something comparable in size to Ant, and in some services even bigger.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1159174\" style=\"width: 764px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1159174\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-1159174\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/05/screen-shot-2015-05-18-at-1-38-19-pm.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"754\" height=\"477\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/05/screen-shot-2015-05-18-at-1-38-19-pm.png 754w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/05/screen-shot-2015-05-18-at-1-38-19-pm.png?resize=150,95 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/05/screen-shot-2015-05-18-at-1-38-19-pm.png?resize=300,190 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/05/screen-shot-2015-05-18-at-1-38-19-pm.png?resize=680,430 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/05/screen-shot-2015-05-18-at-1-38-19-pm.png?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 754px) 100vw, 754px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1159174\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.flickr.com/photos/the_progressive/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">the_progressive <span class=\"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)</span></a> / <a href=\"https://www.flickr.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Flickr <span class=\"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)</span></a> under a <a href=\"http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/2.0/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">CC BY-SA 2.0 <span class=\"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)</span></a> license. (Image has been modified)</p></div></p>\n<h2>How one founder combined edtech and gaming</h2>\n<p>Serial founder <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/why-i-left-edtech-and-got-into-gaming/\">Darshan Somashekar writes</a> that if you want to build a great edtech product, then perhaps it should be a game. Here&#8217;s more, from his guest column for Extra Crunch this week:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Earlier this year, we launched <a href=\"https://solitaired.com/\">Solitaired</a>, a casual gaming platform that ties card games to educational experiences and brain training. We’re still early, but signs are encouraging: Our average time on site is 30 minutes, more than three times that of our earlier business. Even better, users come back often, on average returning more than five times per month. Since we’re now in the gaming space, we should have expected these metrics, but they still blew our expectations away. We’ve also found that the downsides can be mitigated. For example, high engagement has led to strong virality, driving down our CAC and increasing our growth. In-app purchase abuses can be tempting for game developers, but by focusing on user growth KPIs, we don’t have the desire to go down those routes. Lastly, the threat of Big Tech is there, but at present most of their attempts have yet to strike a chord among users. More importantly, that’s why choosing a market so massive that even individual Big Tech players can’t dominate is key: With a market this size, you can shoot for the stars, miss the moon and still do well for yourself.</p></blockquote>\n<h2>Around TechCrunch</h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/pioneers-of-in-space-refueling-and-manufacturing-join-tc-sessions-space-2020/\">Pioneers market, curious about how risk-on, or risk-off things really are today. <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dannycrichton\">Danny</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/nmasc_\">Natasha</a> and <a 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"Update: Springtide, an autism treatment center network, raises $18 million","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073687","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">With one in 54 children diagnosed with autism spectrum disorder in the U.S., the issue of how to treat patients diagnosed with the condition has become almost as acute as the prevalence of the condition itself.</p>\n<p>That&#8217;s one reason why Jia Jia Ye and the team at the healthcare startup studio <a href=\"https://redesignhealth.com/\">Redesign Health</a> were able to raise $18 million in a recent round of funding for the new startup, <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://myspringtide.com/\">Springtide Child Development</a>.*</span></p>\n<p>A longtime executive in the healthcare industry with previous stints at OneMedical and Oscar, Ye and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/redesign-health\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"redesign-health\">Redesign Health&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> team began talking two years ago about potential business ideas. The group settled on autism care because of what they saw as the clear need in the market, Ye said.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;Why this immediately clicked is that the supply and demand imbalance was super clear,&#8221; Ye said. </span></p>\n<p>Simply put, Springtide combines the concierge medical business model with early childcare and education businesses like Sylvan Learning to offer autism care through specialists and a team of registered behavioral technicians.</p>\n<p>To ensure that as many people as possible can use Springtide&#8217;s services the company takes both private insurance and Medicaid.</p>\n<p>So far, the company has one clinic set up in Connecticut providing both remote and in-person services, and it plans to launch several sites throughout the Northeast on the back of its $15.6 million in financing.</p>\n<p>Joining Ye in designing the company&#8217;s facilities and treatment services is Dr. Tiva Pierce, who previously worked at <a href=\"https://www.constellationhs.com/\">Constellation Health Services</a>, which provides behavioral and physical healthcare through schools.</p>\n<p>Like many companies that had an in-person services model, Springtide had to pivot to delivering remote care as soon as the pandemic lockdowns hit the Northeast.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073780\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073780\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2073780\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1134365962.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1134365962.jpg 2121w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1134365962.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1134365962.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/GettyImages-1134365962.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, Getty Images Plus</p></div></p>\n<p>The company charges Medicaid $46 per hour and commercial payers will be charged between $50 and $60 per hour, but the company&#8217;s services will only cost families their typical co-pay and deductible.</p>\n<p>Taking Medicaid was a priority, Ye said, to increase access for more people who need it.</p>\n<p>Already, families in the U.S. spend about $17 billion on ABA therapy, according to Ye. And the overall spending on autism-related issues is $68 billion, she said.</p>\n<p>The financing, which came from <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/deerfield-management-83d0\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"deerfield-management-83d0\">Deerfield Management <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/optum-ventures\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"optum-ventures\">Optum Ventures, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> will be used to expand the company&#8217;s footprint and staff, which currently numbers roughly 30 employees.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“The rapidly growing autism care market is highly fragmented and uncoordinated, which creates significant challenges for children and their families who deserve to have access to care that is consistently of exceptional quality,” said Julian Harris, MD, partner at Deerfield. “Springtide offers an interdisciplinary, in-center care experience with a tech-enabled wrap-around for families who want their children to get all of their care in one setting. With an emphasis on outcomes measurement, we hope that Springtide can serve as a platform for care and research, ultimately establishing the gold standard in this field.</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">”</span></p>\n<p>*<em>This story was updated to indicate that Springtide had closed on $18 million not the $15.6 million originally reported in information provided by the sector that&#8217;s been growing hotter in 2020.</p>\n<p>His post is a unique take on two oft-discussed categories, but it also examines one founder/investor&#8217;s thought process when it comes to evaluating new opportunities.</p>\n<p>Andy Areitio, a partner at early-stage fund TheVentureCity, wrote <a time,&#8221; he says. &#8220;They can also put all their eggs in one basket too early. I made that mistake.&#8221;</p>\n<p>You can find business writing that explores best practices anywhere, which is why we hunt down stories that are firmly rooted in data or personal experience (which 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p>Devin Coldewey interviewed the leaders of three startup accelerators to learn more about the adaptations they&#8217;ve made in recent months:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>David Brown, founder and CEO, Techstars</li>\n<li>Cyril Ebersweiler, founder HAX, venture partner at SOSV</li>\n<li>Daniela Fernandez, founder, Ocean Solutions Accelerator</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Due to travel bans, shelter-in-place orders and other unknowns, they&#8217;ve all shifted to virtual. But accelerators are intensive programs designed to indoctrinate founders and elicit brutally honest feedback in real time.</p>\n<p>Despite the sudden shift, that boot-camp mindset is still in effect, Devin reports.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Cutting out the commute time in a busy city leaves founders with more time for workshops, mentor matchmaking, pitch practice and other important sessions,&#8221; said Fernandez. &#8220;Everybody just has more flexibility and tranquility.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Said Ebersweiler: &#8220;People are for some reason more participative and have more feedback than physically — it’s pretty strange.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"UfO7qJweqy\"><p><a left&#8221; security:</p>\n<p>&#8220;Every organization today wants to bring software to market faster, but they also want to make software more secure,&#8221; said Chandna.</p>\n<p>&#8220;There is a 14:18:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-15 14:18:38","title":"Human Capital: Amazon and CZI face labor disputes as Biden promises gig workers better protections","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073859","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Welcome back to Human Capital. In this week’s edition of HC, you’ll read about the latest labor struggles at Amazon and the Chan Zuckerberg Initiative, President-Elect Joe Biden’s promises to gig workers, a primary care network for Black people and people of color and more. Lastly, I pulled out some nuggets from DoorDash’s S-1 that are relevant to DEI and labor.</p>\n<p>If you want this as an email newsletter every Friday at 1 p.m. PT, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">be sure to sign up here</a>.</p>\n<h3>Former Amazon warehouse worker sues company alleging failure to provide PPE to workers during pandemic</h3>\n<p>Christian Smalls, a former Amazon warehouse employee, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/amazon-faces-lawsuit-alleging-failure-to-provide-ppe-to-workers-during-pandemic/\">filed a lawsuit</a> against the company today alleging Amazon failed to provide personal protective equipment to Black and Latinx workers during the COVID-19 pandemic.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The class action suit alleges Amazon failed to properly protect its warehouse workers and violated elements of New York City’s human rights law, as well as federal and state laws.</p>\n<p>“I was a loyal worker and gave my all to Amazon until I was unceremoniously terminated and tossed aside like yesterday’s trash because I insisted that Amazon protect its dedicated workers from COVID-19,” Smalls said in a statement. “I just wanted Amazon to provide basic protective gear to the workers and sanitize the workplace.”</p>\n<h3>Center for Black Innovation gets $2.1 million</h3>\n<p>The Knight Foundation, Surdna Foundation and Comcast NBCUNiversal <a href=\"https://knightfoundation.org/press/releases/national-foundations-and-global-media-and-technology-company-invest-over-2m-to-increase-black-entrepreneurship-in-the-u-s/\">put $2.1 million into the Center for Black Innovation</a>. The plan is to support Black entrepreneurs and increase the number of Black founders in Miami and throughout the U.S. The money will go toward investor education, facilitating matchmaking sessions between founders and investors, offering courses to founders and more.</p>\n<h3>Chan Zuckerberg Initiative faces racial discrimination complaint</h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1338295\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1338295\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-1338295\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"470\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg 2433w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg?resize=150,104 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg?resize=300,207 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg?resize=768,531 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg?resize=680,470 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg?resize=1536,1062 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg?resize=2048,1416 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/gettyimages-512266184.jpg?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1338295\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">BERLIN, GERMANY &#8211; FEBRUARY 25: (r-l) Mark Zuckerberg, CEO and founder of the social media platform Facebook, and his wife Priscilla Chan pose for a photo before the Axel-Springer-Award on February 25, 2016 in Berlin. Mark Zuckerberg got this first time awarding price for special innovations. (Photo by Florian Gaertner/Photothek via Getty Images)</p></div></p>\n<p>Ray Holgado, a former employee of the Chan Zuckerberg Initiative, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/chan-zuckerberg-initiative-faces-racial-discrimination-allegations-from-former-employee/\">recently filed a racial discrimination complaint with the California Department of Fair Employment and Housing</a>. Holgado, who is Black, worked at CZI from September 2018 through August 2020.</p>\n<p>“Despite its social justice rhetoric, CZI is not a welcoming environment for Black employees,” Holgado’s complaint states. “Black employees are underpaid, undervalued, denied growth opportunities, and marginalized. Black employees who want to advance within the organization are shut down and labeled as too assertive or aggressive, while non-Black employees are favored and encouraged. When Black employees have communicated these concerns to CZI leadership, CZI has responded defensively and failed to address the underlying issues. CZI has utterly failed to ‘build a more inclusive, just, and healthy future’ for its Black employees.”</p>\n<p>In a statement to TechCrunch, CZI denied the claims.</p>\n<p>“While we take any allegation of discrimination seriously and will do so here, this former employee’s specific allegations were previously raised internally, independently investigated, and found to be unsubstantiated,” the spokesperson said. “The Chan Zuckerberg Initiative is committed to fair treatment, access, and advancement for all members of the CZI team. We do not tolerate discrimination of any kind, full stop.”</p>\n<h3>DEI nuggets from DoorDash’s S-1</h3>\n<p>Food delivery company DoorDash filed its paperwork to go public today. It’s a long document, so I’ve pulled out the relevant items related to DEI and labor.</p>\n<p><strong>DoorDash says it’s committed to diversity and inclusion in its S-1, despite never having released a diversity report</strong></p>\n<blockquote><p>At DoorDash, we are committed to growing and empowering inclusive communities in our company, our industry, and the cities we serve. We believe that a diverse and inclusive workforce is critical to helping us attract and retain the talent necessary to grow our business. We also believe we will be a more successful company if we amplify the voices of those who have not always been heard, and when everyone has ‘room at the table’ and the tools, resources, and opportunities to succeed.</p></blockquote>\n<p><strong>DoorDash also seems to be proud of the fact that none of its 3,279 employees have unionized:</strong></p>\n<blockquote><p>None of our employees are represented by a labor union. We have not experienced any work stoppages, and we believe that our employee relations are strong.</p></blockquote>\n<p><strong>DoorDash, like other gig economy companies, is also gearing up to pursue Prop 22-like legislation in other states:</strong></p>\n<blockquote><p>As such, the passage of the 2020 California ballot initiative is likely to have an adverse impact on our results of operations. In addition, several other states where we operate may be considering adopting legislation similar to the 2020 California ballot initiative, which we would expect to increase our costs related to Dashers in such jurisdictions and could also adversely impact our results of operations.</p></blockquote>\n<h3>Spora Health launches primary care provider network for Black people and POC</h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2070773\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2070773\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2070773\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Product-Assets-Press.001.jpeg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Product-Assets-Press.001.jpeg 1920w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Product-Assets-Press.001.jpeg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Product-Assets-Press.001.jpeg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Product-Assets-Press.001.jpeg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Product-Assets-Press.001.jpeg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Product-Assets-Press.001.jpeg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Product-Assets-Press.001.jpeg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2070773\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Spora Health</p></div></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/spora-health-launches-primary-care-network-for-black-people-and-people-of-color/\">Spora Health launched</a> its One Medical-like primary care provider network for Black people and people of color.</p>\n<p>“An equitable healthcare system has never existed in America, especially for Black folks and that is the goal,” Spora Health  founder and CEO Dan Miller told TechCrunch.</p>\n<p>Spora Health, which recently closed a $1.2 million seed round, is a primary care provider for Black people and people of color. Initially, Spora Health is taking a telemedicine approach, but eventually plans to open physical locations.</p>\n<h3>Lyft on passage of Prop 22</h3>\n<p>“As we look to the future, the win on Proposition 22 in California was a landmark achievement and a major victory for drivers, our industry and the broader Lyft community,” <a href=\"https://investor.lyft.com/static-files/adfd1bd4-f094-4724-8b6c-5caf1e5b3fd8\">Lyft President John Zimmer said in Lyft’s earnings report this week</a>. “The campaign was successful because it ultimately reflected the desires and priorities of drivers. More than 120,000 drivers signed up to be part of the effort to pass Prop 22 – they rallied, they volunteered, they shared their stories. Voters saw that and stood in solidarity with them. We look forward to continuing our conversations with policymakers across the country.”</p>\n<p>Similar to Uber, Lyft is also looking to explore similar legislation across the country. On the earnings call, Lyft CEO Logan Green said Prop 22 provides a model for other states.</p>\n<h3>Uber and Lyft request rehearing on case that upheld preliminary injunction</h3>\n<p>Uber and Lyft both filed a petition for rehearings in the case brought forth by California Attorney General Xavier Becerra. Last month, an appeals court upheld a lower court ruling that would force Uber and Lyft to classify their drivers as employees. But now that Proposition 22 has passed, Uber and Lyft want the court to determine if the injunction is still appropriate.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Uber and Lyft will likely still face lawsuits over worker classification in California since the recently-passed proposition can not be applied retroactively. According to Bloomberg Law, <a href=\"https://news.bloomberglaw.com/daily-labor-report/california-gig-workers-still-can-sue-for-wages-after-prop-22\">those legal options</a>, however, will be limited and damages will be capped.</p>\n<h3>Human Rights Watch and Amnesty International on Prop 22</h3>\n<p>In a joint statement, the Human Rights Watch and Amnesty International called Prop 22 a “devastating blow to the rights” of gig workers.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/research/2020/11/california-prop-22-is-a-devastating-blow-to-the-rights-of-app-based-workers/#_edn3\">Here’s a snippet</a>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>No worker should face exploitative or otherwise abusive work conditions, but many app-based workers do. We urge app-based companies to bring their wage and labor policies and practices in line with international human and labor rights standards. We urge the government of California to explore other legal avenues for holding companies accountable for respecting workers’ rights. Finally, we urge the United States Congress and the United States Department of Labor to protect the rights of app-based workers, such as through legislative and regulatory action that helps ensure a living wage, paid sick and family leave, and workers’ compensation for illness and injury.</p></blockquote>\n<div class=\"newsletter__block__header\">\n<h3>Biden promises to get gig workers the “benefits and protections they deserve”</h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2070946\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2070946\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2070946\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Joe Biden and Kamala Harris\" width=\"680\" height=\"463\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg 5000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg?resize=150,102 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg?resize=300,204 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg?resize=768,523 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg?resize=680,463 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg?resize=1536,1047 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg?resize=2048,1396 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/biden-harris-GettyImages-1228132294.jpg?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2070946\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">TOPSHOT &#8211; Former vice-president and Democratic presidential nominee Joe Biden (L) and Senator from California and Democratic vice presidential nominee Kamala Harris greet supporters outside the Chase Center in Wilmington, Delaware, at the conclusion of the Democratic National Convention, held virtually amid the novel coronavirus pandemic, on August 20, 2020. (Photo by Olivier DOULIERY / AFP) (Photo by OLIVIER DOULIERY/AFP via Getty Images)</p></div></p>\n<p>Under President-Elect Joe Biden’s administration, <a href=\"https://joebiden.com/empowerworkers/\">he has promised</a> to “ensure workers in the ‘gig economy’ and beyond receive the legal benefits and protections they deserve,” his transition site states. The administration goes on to describe how gig workers are misclassified and therefore deprived of their rightful benefits and protections.</p>\n<p>“This epidemic of misclassification is made possible by ambiguous legal tests that give too much discretion to employers, too little protection to workers, and too little direction to government agencies and courts,” the site states.</p>\n<p>Moving forward, Biden says he will work with Congress to create a federal standard that is modeled on the ABC test. Whether Biden follows through with that promise, however, has yet to be seen.</p>\n<p>You can <a href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/4adv8g/biden-promised-to-reclassify-gig-workers-but-how-will-he-actually-do-it\">read more</a> about how gig workers feel about the upcoming Biden administration as it relates to labor over on <a href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/4adv8g/biden-promised-to-reclassify-gig-workers-but-how-will-he-actually-do-it\">Vice</a>.</p>\n</div>\n<div id=\"speakable-summary\"><em>This is The TechCrunch Exchange, a newsletter that goes out on Saturdays, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/the-exchange/\">based on the column of the same name</a>. You can sign up for the email <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">here</a>.</em></p>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\">DoorDash filed to go public on Friday, meaning we’ll have at least one more unicorn IPO before 2020 comes to a close. For a high-level look at its numbers, I <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/doordash-files-to-go-public/\">wrote this</a>, Danny covered who <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/the-vc-and-founder-winners-of-doordashs-ipo/\">will profit from the deal</a>, and I noodled on <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/how-covid-19-accelerated-doordashs-business/\">the impact of COVID-19 on its business</a>.</p>\n<p>I bring all that up because there is another COVID-19 impacted unicorn that we are expecting to see go public in very short order: Airbnb.</p>\n<p>When Airbnb <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/19/airbnb-has-confidentially-filed-to-go-public/#:~:text=In%20a%20turn%20of%20fortune,an%20IPO%20filing%20this%20month.\">filed to go public in August</a>, it seemed like a solid plan. The company was widely reported to be <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/understanding-airbnbs-summer-recovery/\">on an upswing from its COVID-doldrums</a>, the public markets <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/16/go-public-now-while-software-valuations-make-no-sense-part-ii/\">were hot for growth and tech shares</a>, and the pandemic’s caseload in the United States was coming down from its summer highs. It looked great for Airbnb to wrap its Q3, drop its public S-1 with the new numbers, and laugh all the way to the bank after showing investors that even a global pandemic and travel industry depression couldn’t stop it.</p>\n<p>And yet. The United States and world at large are now in the midst of the worst COVID-19 spike yet, and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Kr00ney/status/1327339099917873152\">consumer spend is going down</a> right before we get the company’s S-1. November feels less winsome for an Airbnb recovery than August or September did. Still, when Airbnb files &#8212; next week, the scuttlebutt indicates, so get ready &#8212; we’ll only have a look at its numbers through the third quarter.</p>\n<p>That’s effectively the same timeframe for a dataset that the folks at <a href=\"https://www.cardify.ai/\">Cardify</a> sent over and I dug through. Per the company, which tracks real-time consumer spend data, here’s a look at how well Airbnb recovered ahead of its larger industry after the initial recession in pandemic lodging spend:</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-2073950 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.24-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"621\" height=\"243\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.24-PM.png 621w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.24-PM.png?resize=150,59 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.24-PM.png?resize=300,117 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.24-PM.png?resize=50,20 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 621px) 100vw, 621px\" /></p>\n<p>Impressive, right? Sadly for Airbnb, the initial boom of demand through late June into July tapered as time continued.</p>\n<p>Zooming in somewhat, here’s Airbnb spend data from July 2020 through the end of October, the first month of Q4, compared to the same period of 2019:</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-2073951\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.39-PM.png?w=620\" alt=\"\" width=\"620\" height=\"242\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.39-PM.png 620w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.39-PM.png?resize=150,59 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.39-PM.png?resize=300,117 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-13-at-3.06.39-PM.png?resize=50,20 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 620px) 100vw, 620px\" /></p>\n<p>Declines, then, but still an encouraging set of data for the company regardless. I would not have expected Airbnb spend &#8212; via third-party, admittedly &#8212; to be this strong.</p>\n<p>The trend of folks renting a house for a month seems to have diminished somewhat, in case you are factoring that into your mental math concerning Airbnb revenues from the above charts. Cardify told TechCrunch that after peaking at around +70% in the March-April timeframe, “average booking sizes have now normalized and are approximately 30% higher on a YTD basis.”</p>\n<p>There is weakness in October, the charts show, but that appears to be at least partially seasonal given the 2019 line, so I don’t want to over-ascribe rising COVID cases as the cause. The drooping line, however, was echoed in similar <a href=\"https://www.similarweb.com/\">SimilarWeb</a> data that was also shared with The Exchange. The dataset concerned accommodation booking volume around the world for a number of travel services, including Airbnb. Its data tracking the US market showed that a bookings recovery through September that made up some ground on March lows was undercut by October declines. Europe’s bookings’ recovery peaked in July and has been falling ever since. Asian volume is creeping higher, but down sharply from prior levels.</p>\n<p>It was a mixed picture, but as Airbnb is doing better than its broader industry per Cardify, the aggregated data could be leading us to be more pessimistic than we otherwise need to be. We’ll see shortly what the real numbers are, but I couldn&#8217;t help but share what I was reading with you. On to the S-1!</p>\n<p><em>Before DoorDash filed, we were going to talk about Brex today in this space after Airbnb. But, since we got extra busy, expect those notes early next week on The Exchange.</em></p>\n<h2>Market Notes</h2>\n<p><em>The week was super busy with earnings, so I’ve collected a few notes from calls with select companies after they reported. Apologies to everyone&#8217;s’ favorite reporting firm, but we’re space-limited.</em></p>\n<p><strong>Appian</strong> <a href=\"https://seekingalpha.com/news/3633206-appianplus-15-on-earnings-smasher-provides-q4-and-fy-guidance\">crushed</a> earnings expectations. What drove the low-code application development services’ growth forward? According to CEO Matt Calkins, it wasn’t a single thing. Instead, the company’s performance was driven by a long ramp he said, though he did also state that the concept of low-code has reached the public consciousness in new, higher levels during the last few quarters.</p>\n<p>Why? The year’s chaos pushed companies into new patterns faster than they had anticipated. Chalk this result up to the accelerating digital transformation being real, which is good news for startups. (For more on Appian and the low-code space, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/27/covid-19-is-driving-demand-for-low-code-apps/\">head here</a>.)</p>\n<p><strong>Alteryx</strong> gave The Exchange an earnings first, providing both its newly former CEO Dean Stoecker and its new CEO Mark Anderson to chat results. The company <a href=\"https://seekingalpha.com/news/3632548-alteryx-eps-beats-0_25-beats-on-revenue\">crushed Q3 expectations</a>, but its Q4 <a href=\"https://seekingalpha.com/news/3633215-sell-side-weighs-in-alteryx-tumbles-on-soft-q4-outlook\">projections</a> did not excite investors. What was up? Anderson argued that ARR growth, not forward GAAP revenue projections, is the most transparent and clear view of an expanding software company, to paraphrase his thinking. You can’t ignore revenue, he said, but given the nuances in how revenue is counted, pay attention to ARR.</p>\n<p>Alteryx has a solid ARR target for 2021. We’ll see how investors view its Q4 results and if they align their thinking to that of the new CEO. Alteryx’s former CEO is bullish, saying that in time the market will realize that analytics is at the epicenter of digital transformation. And his company will be there with code to sell.</p>\n<p>Moving along, earlier this week I <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/5-vcs-discuss-the-future-of-saas-and-software-after-pfizers-vaccine-breakthrough/\">asked a number of VCs about the software venture capital market</a> in the wake of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/positive-vaccine-news-punishes-pandemic-boosted-companies-like-zoom-peloton-etsy/\">Monday’s sharp selloff</a> and my question about <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/what-happens-to-high-flying-startups-if-the-pandemic-trade-flips/\">what might happen to public and private software companies</a> if other stocks suddenly became more attractive &#8212; strong vaccine news on Monday was later overwhelmed by surging cases as the week went along, but on Monday Zoom lost billions in value as investors fled.</p>\n<p>One set of responses came in late, but I wanted to share them all the same as they were more bullish than I anticipated. In the view of <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/laela-sturdy-376543/\">Laela Sturdy</a>, a general partner at Alphabet <strong>Capital G</strong>, “private software investors are unlikely to change their investing patterns much as a result of fluctuations in the public market,” adding later that “public market changes would have to be very extreme &#8212; as in 30 percent or more &#8212; in order to impact growth stage valuations.”</p>\n<p>The connection between public valuations and trading patterns and private capital deployment exists, but how closely the two are linked depends on what’s happening at any given moment, and it appears that at the moment private investor excitement about software is durable.</p>\n<p>Sturdy explained why that may be: “Long-term secular trends around cloud adoption, automation and AI, data, security, fintech infrastructure, and the ongoing rapid acceleration of digital transformation will help tech companies maintain their status as the darlings of growth investors in both the private and public markets.”</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Hopin raised $125 million at a $2.125 billion valuation after scaling to $20 million in ARR in under a year. Wow.</li>\n<li>Square and PayPal earnings <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/11/square-and-paypal-earnings-bring-good-and-bad-news-for-fintech-startups/\">augur well for fintech startups overall</a>, though it appears that most fintech money is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/fintech-vc-keeps-getting-later-larger-and-more-expensive/\">going to only the latest-stages of that niche</a>. (<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/truebill-series-c/\">TrueBill just raised $17 million, notably</a>.)</li>\n<li>Udemy <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/13/filing-online-learning-marketplace-udemy-is-raising-up-to-100m-at-a-3-32b-valuation/\">wants $100 million more</a>.</li>\n<li>What’s <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/as-public-investors-reprice-edtech-bets-whats-ahead-for-the-hot-startup-sector/\">ahead for edtech startups</a> now that edtech stocks are taking hits?</li>\n<li>Menlo Security <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/menlo-security-announces-100m-series-e-on-800m-valuation/\">landed $100 million more at an $800 million valuation</a>. Not bad!</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Various and Sundry</h2>\n<p>And finally, the rest of the stuff that I couldn’t get to this week. Here we go:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Chatted with <a href=\"https://www.cic.vc/\">Cambridge Innovation Capital</a>, a neat venture capital firm from Cambridge in the U.K. &#8212; not the Cambridge on the American East Coast. More to say here, but the good news is that hubs of innovation really are maturing into startup factories the world around.</li>\n<li>I got my hands on an early copy of a survey of LPs put together by <a href=\"https://allocate.gp/\">Allocate</a>. It comes out Monday I think, but it said that “only 20% of [LP] respondents said COVID had slowed their investment activities,” which helps explain all the funds we’ve seen in the past few months.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Closing with something fun, remember that look we did of the performance of various startups in Q3? That was fun. Anyhoo, no-code “online form builder” <a href=\"https://www.jotform.com/\">JotForm</a> told The Exchange that its revenue is up 50% from its 2019 results, that its enterprise customer base is up 620%, and that it expects to reach “100,000 total paid users by end of year.” Neat!</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/alex\">Alex</a></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
